مبحث العام
بيان حكم العام

فسألها عن أعماله فقالت: كان يرعى الغنم، ولا يتنزه من بوله، فحينئذ قال عليه استنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه فهو بحسب شأن النزول أيضًا خاص ببول ما يؤكل لحمه كما كان المنسوخ خاصا به لكن العبرة لعموم اللفظ، لا لخصوص السبب والذي يدل على كون حديث العرنيين منسوحًا بهذا الحديث أن المثلة التي تضمنها حديث: العرنيين منسوخة بالاتفاق؛ لأنها كانت في ابتداء الإسلام. تأييد وإذا أوصى بخاتم لإنسان، ثم بالفص منه لآخر، أن الحلقة للأول، والفص بينهما، تأيـ لمقدمة مفهومة مما قبل وهي أن العام مساوٍ للخاص بمسألة فقهية، وهي أنه إذا أوصى : به: أي ببول ما يؤكل لحمه. (القمر) والذي يدل إلخ جواب سؤال مقدر تقريره: أن دعوى النسخ إنما تصح إذا ثبت تقدم حديث العرنيين، وتأخر حديث الاستنزاه من البول، ولم يثبت؛ إذ لم يعرف التاريخ. وحاصل الجواب: أن انتساخ حديث العرنيين ثابت بدليل أن المثلة التي تضمنها هذا الحديث كانت مشروعة في بدء الإسلام، ثم نسخت بالاتفاق بحديث طويل رواه الترمذي عن بريدة، وخلاصته : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا بعث أميرًا على جيش أوصاه بوصايا، ويقول: اغزوا ولا تغلوا ولا تغدروا، ولا تمثلوا، فدل انتساخها على انتساخ هذا الحديث وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن حديث العرنيين متضمن للحكمين المثلة وشرب أبوال الإبل، وانتساخ الأول أي المثلة لا يستلزم انتساخ الثاني أي شرب أبوال الإبل. فالجواب الحق أن حديث الاستنزاه من البول محرم، وحديث العرنيين مبيح، والمحرم هو المتأخر كيلا يتكرر النسخ وهو نسخ الإباحة الأصلية بالمحرم، ثم نسخ المحرم بالمبيح على ما تقرر في موضعه فثبت تقدم حديث العرينين تدبر (القمر) التي يعني كون جزاء القتل والاستراق ما جاء في الحديث. (المحشي) بمسألة فقهية ذكرها الإمام محمد في "الزيادات" كذا قيل. (القمر) أما القصة فلم أجدها هذا اللفظ [إشراق الأبصار (۸] وأخرج الدار قطني في "سننه" ۱۲۸/۱، باب نجاسة البول والأمر بالتنزه منه والحكم في بول ما يؤكل لحمه، عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: استنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه الصواب مرسل، وفي رواية لأنس تترهوا من البول ويعضد القصة ما روى البخاري رقم: ۲۱۵ باب من الكبائر أن لا يستتر من بوله ومسلم رقم ۲۹۲ باب الدليل على نجاسة البول ووجوب الاستنزاه منه، عن ابن عباس قال: مر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بقبرين، فقال: إنهما ليعذبان وما يعذبان في كبير أما أحدهما، فكان لا يستتر من البول، وأما الآخر فكان يمشي بالنميمة.

مبحث العام
بيان حكم العام

أحد بخاتمه لإنسان، ثم أوصى بكلام مفصول بعده بفص ذلك الخاتم بعينه لإنسان آخر، فتكون الحلقة للموصى له الأول خاصةً، والفص مشتركًا بين الأول والثاني على السواء؛ وذلك لأن الخاتم عام أي كالعام؛ لأن العام المصطلح هو: ما يشمل أفرادا، لا عام بعينه والخاتم لا يصدق إلا على فرد واحد، ولكنه كالعام يشمل الحلقة والفص كليهما، والفص خاص بمدلوله فقط، فإذا ذكر الخاص بعد العام بكلام مفصول وقع التعارض للفصل بين الكلامين بينهما في حق الفص، فيكون الفص للموصى لهما جميعًا تسوية للعام مع الخاص، بخلاف ما إذا أوصى بالفص بكلام موصول، فإنه يكون بيانًا؛ لأن المراد بالخاتم فيما سبق: الحلقة فقط، فتكون الحلقة للأول والفص للثاني، وعند أبي يوسف الله يكون الفص للثاني البتة سواء أتى بكلام موصول أو مفصول؛ لأن الوصية إنما تلزم بعد مماته لا في حياته، فكان الموصول والمفصول سواء الموصي بكلام مفصول هذا القيد يفهم من المتن بدلالة لفظة "ثم" . (القمر) أي كالعام إنما فسر بهذا؛ لئلا يتجه أن العام ما يتناول أفرادا متفقة الحدود، والخاتم ليس كذلك، وشموله للفص شمول للجزء، ولا يصير اللفظ باعتبار الأجزاء عاما، فيكون الخاتم والفص كلاهما خاصين، فلا يستقيم التأييد. (القمر)
وقع التعارض: إذا لا يمكن جعل الوصية الثانية تخصيصا للأولى؛ لعدم المقارنة بينهما حقيقة، والمخصص لابد أن يكون مقارنا. (القمر) في حق الفص إلخ لأن الإيصاء بخاتم يستدعي أن يكون الفص أيضًا للإنسان كالحلقة، والإيصاء بعده بالفص فقط لآخر يقتضي أن يكون لآخر ، فوقع التعارض فيه لا في الحلقة. (السنبلي) تسوية للعام الخ: أي ليتحقق العمل بكل واحد منهما ، ولا يفوت العمل بأحد منهما، وإلا لزم التفريق بينهما، فلا يجوز أن يعمل بالخاص، ويكون الفص لآخر فقط، ويترك العمل بالعام أي لا يكون الفص لإنسان أصلاً؛ لأن العام أيضًا يوجب الحكم فيما يتناوله كالخاص. (السنبلي) فإنه يكون بيانًا إلخ فالإيصاء الثاني تخصيص للأول؛ لتحقق شرط التخصيص وهو المقارنة. (القمر) وعند أبي يوسف إلخ ذكر شمس الأئمة في "زياداته"، وأبو زيد في "التقويم" وفخر الإسلام على البزدوي هذه المسألة من غير ذكر خلاف أبي يوسف له رواية شاذة. (القمر)
Section on the General. Statement of the ruling of the general. He asked her about his actions, and she said: He used to tend sheep and did not protect himself from his urine. So then he (peace be upon him) said: Protect yourselves from urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it. So it is also specifically about the urine of animals whose meat is eaten, just as the abrogated was specific to it. But consideration is for the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the cause. And what indicates that the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun is abrogated by this hadith is that the mutilation which that hadith contains is abrogated by consensus, because it was at the beginning of Islam. Support: And if one bequeaths a ring to a person, then the gemstone from it to another, then the ring is for the first, and the gemstone is between them. Support for a premise understood from what precedes, namely that the general is equal to the specific in a fiqh issue, which is that if one bequeaths: by it, meaning urine of animals whose meat is eaten. (Al-Qamar) And what indicates etc. is the answer to an implied question: that the claim of abrogation is only valid if the precedence of the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun and the lateness of the hadith of avoidance from urine is established, and it is not established because the date is unknown. The summary of the answer: that the abrogation of the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun is established by the evidence that the mutilation contained in this hadith was permissible at the beginning of Islam, then abrogated by consensus by a long hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi from Buraydah, the gist of which is: that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he sent a commander on an expedition, would advise him with instructions and say: Fight and do not embezzle, do not treacher, and do not mutilate. So its abrogation indicates the abrogation of this hadith. And it should not be hidden from you that the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun contains two rulings: mutilation and drinking camel urine, and the abrogation of the first (mutilation) does not necessitate the abrogation of the second (drinking camel urine). So the correct answer is that the hadith of avoidance from urine is prohibitive, and the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun is permissive, and the prohibitive is later to avoid repeated abrogation, and it is abrogation of the original permissibility by the prohibitive, then abrogation of the prohibitive by the permissive, as established in its place. So the precedence of the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun is established. Reflect. (Al-Qamar) That means the penalty for killing and stealing is what came in the hadith. (Al-Muhashi) Regarding a fiqh issue mentioned by Imam Muhammad in al-Ziyadat, it is said. (Al-Qamar) As for the story, I did not find it in these words. al-Daraqutni narrated in his Sunan: book of impurity of urine and the order to avoid it and the ruling on urine of what is eaten, from Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Avoid urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it. The correct is that it is mursal. And in a narration from Anas: Cleanse yourselves from urine. The story is supported by what al-Bukhari narrated: chapter on major sins not to protect oneself from urine, and Muslim: chapter on the evidence of impurity of urine and the obligation of avoiding it, from Ibn Abbas who said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, passed by two graves and said: They are being punished, and not for a great thing: as for one, he did not protect himself from urine; and the other, he used to go about with slander.

Section on the General. Statement of the ruling of the general. One to his ring to a person, then he bequeathed with separate speech afterwards the gemstone of that same ring to another person, then the ring is exclusively for the first legatee, and the gemstone is shared equally between the first and second. That is because the ring is general, i.e., like general, because the technical general is that which encompasses individuals, not a specific general. And the ring is only true of one individual, but it is like general in that it encompasses both the ring and the gemstone, and the gemstone is specific in its indication only. So when the specific is mentioned after the general with separate speech, conflict arises between them regarding the gemstone, so the gemstone is for both legatees equally, treating the general and the specific equally. Unlike if he bequeaths the gemstone with connected speech, then it is a clarification, because the intended meaning of the ring previously was only the ring, so the ring is for the first and the gemstone for the second. According to Abu Yusuf, the gemstone is exclusively for the second whether he came with connected or separate speech, because the will is only binding after his death, not during his life, so connected and separate are the same. The condition of separate speech is understood from the text by the indication of the word 'then'. (Al-Qamar) i.e., it is interpreted as like general to prevent the objection that general is what encompasses individuals with identical boundaries, and the ring is not like that, and its inclusion of the gemstone is inclusion of a part, and a word does not become general by virtue of parts, so both ring and gemstone are specific, and the support would not be sound. (Al-Qamar) Conflict occurs: because it is not possible to make the second will a specification of the first, due to lack of temporal connection between them in reality, and the specifying element must be connected. (Al-Qamar) Regarding the gemstone, etc. because bequeathing a ring necessitates that the gemstone also belongs to the first, and bequeathing afterwards the gemstone only to another requires that it be for the other, so conflict occurs in it, not in the ring. (Al-Sunbuliy) Equalizing the general etc.: meaning to verify the operation of each of them, and not to miss operation of either, otherwise separation would be necessitated between them, and it is not permissible to act by the specific, making the gemstone only for the other, and to abandon acting by the general, i.e., the gemstone not belonging to anyone at all, because the general also necessitates the ruling in what it encompasses like the specific. (Al-Sunbuliy) Then it would be a clarification etc. So the second will is a specification of the first, because the condition of specification is met, which is connection. (Al-Qamar) According to Abu Yusuf etc. Shams al-A'imma in his Ziyadat, Abu Zayd in al-Taqwim, and Fakhr al-Islam on al-Bazdawi mentioned this issue without mentioning the difference of Abu Yusuf, as it is a rare transmission. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the ruling of the general term (العام) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, with a practical example from fiqh. The author begins by citing a hadith where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) commands people to avoid urine, stating that most punishment of the grave is due to it. The commentary notes that this command, despite its general wording, is specifically about the urine of animals whose meat is eaten, just as the abrogated ruling was specific to it. However, the principle is reaffirmed: the legal consideration is for the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the occasion of revelation (العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب). This is a foundational rule in Hanafi usul. The passage then addresses the apparent conflict between this hadith and the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun, which permitted drinking camel urine. The commentator explains that the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun is abrogated by consensus regarding mutilation, but that does not necessitate abrogation of the permission to drink urine. Instead, the correct understanding is that the hadith commanding avoidance is prohibitive and later, while the 'Urayniyyun hadith is permissive and earlier, thus establishing a chronological order without repeated abrogation. The main legal example is the case of a will: a person bequeaths a ring (خاتم) to one person, then separately bequeaths the gemstone (فص) of that same ring to another. According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, since the word 'ring' is general encompassing both the band and the gemstone, and the second bequest is separate (with a disconnected utterance), both bequests are operative on the gemstone, so it becomes shared equally between the two legatees. If the second bequest had been connected (e.g., 'and its gemstone to X'), it would be a specification, giving the gemstone solely to the second. However, Abu Yusuf holds that because a will takes effect only after death, the connection or disconnection makes no difference, and the gemstone goes entirely to the second legatee. The commentary considers Abu Yusuf's view as a rare transmission (رواية شاذة).

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A term that encompasses multiple individuals or parts, like 'ring' encompassing band and gemstone.
خاص (khāṣṣ): A term that indicates a specific individual or part, like 'gemstone' indicating only that part.
موصول (mawṣūl): Connected speech, where the specific mention is directly linked to the general without a break.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man bequeaths his ring to Zaid, then in a separate utterance bequeaths the gemstone of that same ring to Amr. According to the majority Hanafi view, who gets the gemstone?
A) Zaid gets the entire ring including gemstone
B) Amr gets the gemstone exclusively
C) Zaid and Amr share the gemstone equally
D) The gemstone is returned to the estate

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wills, a specific bequest after a general one specifies only if connected; otherwise, the specific object is shared.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
General and Specific in Bequests: The Ring Analogy and the Condition of Connection
Explaining general and specific bequests with ring and slave analogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that disconnected speech prevents specification (takhsis) by analysing the ring bequest example and distinguishing between connected and disconnected bequests.

Core Idea
A disconnected specific bequest cannot override a general one; the specific item is shared.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi usul example: a person bequeaths a ring to one person, then later bequeaths its stone to another with disconnected speech. The ruling hinges on whether the second bequest can specify the first. The Hanafi school insists that specification (takhsis) requires the specifier to be connected to the general term. We will see how this principle plays out in practice and why Abu Yusuf disagreed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Basic Scenario and Terms
Identify the two bequests: (1) a ring (general, covering band and stone), (2) the stone (specific). Note the speech is disconnected (the word 'then' indicates a gap).
2
Distinguish Connected vs. Disconnected Speech
If the second bequest is connected (e.g., 'and its stone'), it specifies the first; the first gets only the band. If disconnected, conflict arises.
Connection means the specific is mentioned without any intervening word or pause.
3
Apply the Hanafi Condition of Connection for Takhsis
Hanafi usul holds that a general term remains general until a connected specifier appears. Disconnection prevents specification, so both bequests are valid and conflict over the stone must be resolved by sharing.
This is derived from the principle that 'amm is qat'i until takhsis.
4
Note the Disagreement of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf argues that wills take effect only after death, so connection/disconnection at the time of bequest is irrelevant. He gives the stone solely to the second legatee in all cases.
Abu Yusuf's view is a rare transmission (shadhdhah).
5
Extend to the Slave Person/Service Example
If one bequeaths a slave's person (رقبة) to one and its service (خدمة) to another, no conflict arises because person and service are different categories. This contrasts with the ring, where stone is part of the ring.
This shows that the ring example is about partial inclusion, not categorical difference.

(القمر) أي كالعام إنما فسر بهذا؛ لئلا يتجه أن العام ما يتناول أفرادا متفقة الحدود، والخاتم ليس كذلك، وشموله للفص شمول للجزء، ولا يصير اللفظ باعتبار الأجزاء عاما، فيكون الخاتم والفص كلاهما ،خاصين، فلا يستقيم التأييد. (القمر) وقع التعارض: إذا لا يمكن جعل الوصية الثانية تخصيصا للأولى؛ لعدم المقارنة بينهما حقيقة، والمخصص لابد أن يكون مقارنا. (القمر) في حق الفص إلخ لأن الإيصاء بخاتم يستدعي أن يكون الفص أيضًا للإنسان كالحلقة، والإيصاء بعده بالفص فقط لآخر يقتضي أن يكون لآخر ، فوقع التعارض فيه لا في الحلقة. (السنبلي) تسوية للعام الخ: أي ليتحقق العمل بكل واحد منهما ، ولا يفوت العمل بأحد منهما، وإلا لزم التفريق بينهما، فلا يجوز أن يعمل بالخاص، ويكون الفص لآخر فقط، ويترك العمل بالعام أي لا يكون الفص لإنسان أصلاً؛ لأن العام أيضًا يوجب الحكم فيما يتناوله كالخاص. (السنبلي) فإنه يكون بيانًا إلخ فالإيصاء الثاني تخصيص للأول؛ لتحقق شرط التخصيص وهو المقارنة. (القمر) وعند أبي يوسف إلخ ذكر شمس الأئمة في "زياداته"، وأبو زيد في "التقويم" وفخر الإسلام على البزدوي هذه المسألة من غير ذكر خلاف أبي يوسف له رواية شاذة. (القمر)
مبحث العام ١٩٤ بيان حكم العام كما في الوصية بالرقبة ،لإنسان وبخدمتها لآخر، قلنا الوصية بالرقبة لا تتناول الخدمة؛ لأنهما الرقبة والخدمة جنسان مختلفان بخلاف الخاتم؛ فإنه يتناول الفص لا محالة، فيكون كالقياس مع الفارق.
Statement of the ruling of the general term: If someone bequeaths a ring to a person, then later bequeaths the stone of that same ring to another person with disconnected speech, then the ring band goes solely to the first legatee, and the stone is shared equally between the first and the second. That is because the ring is general, i.e., like a general term; for the technical general term is what includes individuals, not a particular general, and the ring applies to only one individual, but it is like a general term in that it includes both the band and the stone. The stone is specific to its meaning only. So when the specific is mentioned after the general with disconnected speech, conflict arises due to the separation between the two speeches, regarding the stone, so the stone goes to both legatees equally, treating the general and the specific equally. Contrary to if he bequeaths the stone with connected speech, then it is a specification; because the intended meaning of the ring previously was only the band, so the band goes to the first and the stone to the second. According to Abu Yusuf, may Allah be pleased with him, the stone goes absolutely to the second whether he came with connected or disconnected speech; because a will only takes effect after death, not during his life, so connected and disconnected are the same. (al-Qamar) "With disconnected speech" this condition is understood from the text by the indication of the word "then". (al-Qamar) i.e., "like a general term" is interpreted this way to avoid the objection that the general term includes individuals with the same boundaries, but the ring is not like that, and its inclusion of the stone is inclusion of a part, and a word does not become general by virtue of its parts, thus the ring and the stone would both be specific, so the analogy would not be sound. (al-Qamar) Conflict arises: because it is impossible to make the second will a specification of the first due to the lack of real connection, and a specifier must be connected. (al-Qamar) Regarding the stone etc.: because bequeathing a ring requires that the stone also goes to the first person like the band, and bequeathing after it only the stone to another requires that it goes to the other, so conflict arises in it, not in the band. (al-Sunbuli) Treating the general and specific equally: i.e., to realize the operation of each of them, and not to miss the operation of one of them; otherwise, it would necessitate differentiation between them, so it is not permissible to act on the specific and give the stone only to the other and abandon acting on the general, meaning the stone not going to the first person at all; because the general also necessitates the ruling regarding what it covers like the specific. (al-Sunbuli) Then it is a specification etc.: because the second will is a specification of the first due to the fulfillment of the condition of specification, which is connection. (al-Qamar) And according to Abu Yusuf etc.: Shams al-A'imma mentioned in his "Ziyadat" and Abu Zayd in "al-Taqwim" and Fakhr al-Islam on al-Bazdawi mentioned this case without mentioning the disagreement of Abu Yusuf, for him there is a rare narration. (al-Qamar)
Section on the General 194 Statement of the ruling of the general term as in the bequest of the slave's person to a person and its service to another: We say, the bequest of the person does not include the service; because the person and the service are two different categories, contrary to the ring; for it includes the stone necessarily, so it is like an analogy with a difference.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the ruling of general terms (عام) in the context of wills. It begins with an example: a person bequeaths a ring (خاتم) to one person, then later bequeaths the stone (فص) of that same ring to another. If the second bequest is made with disconnected speech (مفصول), the ring's band goes solely to the first, but the stone is shared equally. This is because the first bequest is considered like a general term (كالعام) covering both band and stone, while the second is specific. When specific follows general with a disconnect, it cannot specify the general; conflict arises and is resolved by giving both equal share in the stone. If connected (موصول), the second specifies the first: the first gets only the band, the second gets the stone. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the stone always goes to the second regardless of connection, because wills take effect only after death. The commentary then counters a potential objection: the ring is not a true general term (since it is one object), but it functions like one because it includes parts. The conflict in the stone is resolved by treating both bequests equally to avoid nullifying either. The passage ends with a related example: if one bequeaths a slave's person (رقبة) to one and its service (خدمة) to another, there is no conflict because the terms are different categories, unlike the ring which includes the stone. This is a distinction (فارق) in the analogy.

Key Terms
العام (al-‘amm): A term that includes multiple individuals; here the ring is 'like a general term' because it includes band and stone.
الخاص (al-khass): A term with a single meaning; here the stone is specific to its own referent.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Making a general term specific by a connected indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the ring bequest example, what is the ruling if the stone is bequeathed with disconnected speech?
A) The stone goes only to the first legatee
B) The stone goes only to the second legatee
C) The stone is shared equally
D) The stone goes to the second if connected, otherwise null

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a specific bequest that is disconnected from a general bequest cannot specify it; the specific item is shared between both legatees.

Specification vs. Abrogation: The Shafi‘i Objection on Quran 6:121
Presenting and refuting the Shafi'i objection that Hanafis inconsistently apply specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a general term (amm) once specified cannot be further specified if doing so would abrogate the original ruling, using Quran 6:121 as a case study.

Core Idea
Specifying a general term so that no case remains under it is abrogation, not permissible specification.

This passage tackles a key usul al-fiqh dispute: the Shafi‘i school argues that since the Hanafis already specified the general prohibition in Quran 6:121 for the forgetful person, they should consistently specify it for the intentional case by analogy or solitary hadith. The Hanafi response reveals a crucial principle: a general term that has already been partially specified cannot be further reduced if doing so would effectively nullify the original command, because that would amount to abrogation (naskh), which requires stronger evidence. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) in slaughter rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term and its coverage
In Quran 6:121, the word 'ma' is a general term covering all cases where Allah's name is not mentioned. According to the Hanafi principle, 'amm is qat'i in its coverage of all its individuals unless specified. Determine which cases fall under it initially: intentional and forgetful omission.
The forgetful was originally included in the general prohibition.
2
Understand the Shafi‘i objection
The Shafi‘i claims that since the Hanafis have already specified (takhsis) the forgetful case out, they have admitted that specification is possible. Therefore, they should also specify the intentional case by analogy or by the solitary hadith 'a Muslim slaughters'. Pinpoint the logical structure of the objection.
The Shafi‘i assumes the forgetful exclusion is a true takhsis.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation: first argument (naskh)
The Hanafi response argues that specifying the intentional case would leave the verse with no practical application (since the only remaining case is the forgetful, which is already excluded). This would fully remove the ruling of the Book, which is abrogation, and abrogation cannot be based on a solitary report or qiyas. Understand the distinction between partial specification (which leaves the ruling applicable to other individuals) and full nullification.
Specification removes some individuals; abrogation removes the ruling entirely.
4
Analyze the Hanafi second argument: forgetful is not specified
The Hanafis clarify that the forgetful person was never truly within the scope of the general term because the Law treats him as if he remembered (due to hardship and the Quranic principle in 2:286). Thus, the forgetful case is not a specification but a legal dispensation. This defuses the Shafi‘i claim of inconsistency.
The forgetful is in the ruling of the dhakir (one who remembered), so he never fell under the general prohibition.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Based on the Hanafi position, the intentional omission renders the meat haram, while the forgetful omission renders it halal. For the Shafi‘i, if they accept specification by analogy or hadith, the intentional omission would also be halal. State the practical difference clearly.
This difference affects actual slaughter practice: Hanafis require Bismillah intentionally; Shafi‘is deem it halal if omitted unintentionally or under duress.

Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi‘i regarding the general term (عام) in the Quranic verse: "Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned" (6:121). The Shafi‘i argues that the word "ما" is general, covering both intentional (عامد) and forgetful (ناسي) omission of the name, and that the Hanafis have inconsistently specified only the forgetful case without specifying the intentional. The Shafi‘i suggests that by analogy or by a solitary hadith (like 'a Muslim slaughters'), the intentional case could also be specified. The Hanafi response is twofold: First, specifying the intentional case would completely remove the ruling of the verse, which is abrogation (نسخ), and abrogation cannot be based on a solitary report. Second, the forgetful person is not actually specified from the verse; rather, the Law treats him as if he remembered (i.e., his meat is halal) to avoid hardship, based on the Quranic verse about not punishing for forgetting (2:286). Thus the forgetful was never part of the general ruling. The text also clarifies that the general term is further restricted by context (دلالة السوق) to slaughtered animals, and this restriction is not technical specification (تخصيص) but simply the intended meaning. The passage ends with a note on Malik's position.

Key Terms
العام (al-‘amm): A word that includes all members of a category; here 'ma' is general for all cases where Allah's name is not mentioned.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Excluding some individuals from the generality of a term by an independent proof.
الناسي (al-nasi): One who forgets to mention Allah's name when slaughtering.
العامد (al-‘amid): One who intentionally omits mentioning Allah's name.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation; the removal of a legal ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the word 'ma' is not a general term
D) Because the intentional omission is permissible by consensus

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between legal dispensation (rukhsah) and specification (takhsis) preserves the general prohibition while accommodating unavoidable forgetfulness, preventing the nullification of a Quranic command by weaker evidence.

Specification of the General 'Man' in 3:97: Qiyas Ma'a al-Fariq
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i specification of the general in 3:97

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'qiyas ma'a al-fariq' to distinguish between valid and invalid analogies, specifically in the context of the promise of security in the Kaaba (Quran 3:97).

Core Idea
An analogy is invalid when the effective cause (illah) differs, even if the cases appear similar.

In this passage, the Hanafi school responds to the Shafi'i argument that the general term 'man' in Quran 3:97 should be specified uniformly across all cases involving the Kaaba. The Shafi'i proposes an analogy between different scenarios, but the Hanafis demonstrate that the analogy fails because the underlying legal cause—sanctity vs. violation—differs. This lesson walks you through that usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and its general term
Locate the Quranic verse (3:97) and the word 'man' (whoever). Understand that the Hanafis accept its generality but have already specified two exceptions based on violation of the Kaaba's sanctity.
The two exceptions are: (1) killing inside the Kaaba after entering, and (2) entering after mutilation.
2
Understand the Shafi'i specification claim
The Shafi'i argues that the third case (entering after killing outside) should be specified by analogy to the first two, because all three involve the Kaaba.
The Shafi'i also cites a solitary report (khabar wahid) to support the specification.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: qiyas ma'a al-fariq
The Hanafis reject the analogy because the first two cases involve violating the sanctity of the Kaaba (harming inside or entering with mutilation), while the third case involves one who honors the Kaaba by seeking refuge. Thus, the effective cause (illah) differs, making the analogy invalid.
This is a classic example of qiyas ma'a al-fariq—the analogy fails due to a fundamental difference in the effective cause.
4
Evaluate the solitary report (khabar wahid)
The Hanafis note that the solitary report cited by the Shafi'i is not strong enough to override the general text, especially when the analogy is already invalid.
The hadith cited at the end of the passage (about slaughtering) is tangential and does not affect this dispute.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The Hanafi position: a murderer who enters the Kaaba after killing outside is secure and cannot be retaliated against inside. The Shafi'i position: he can be retaliated against by analogy.
This difference arises from the usul principle of how to handle general texts and analogies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقرير الثاني: أن في قوله تعالى: وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِنا كلمة "من" أيضًا عامة شاملة لمن

And presentation of the second: that in His statement, 'And whoever enters it is secure' (3:97), the word 'man' is also general, including everyone who enters the house after killing a person, or after cutting off his limbs, or enters the house and then kills someone inside. So it should be that each of these is secure, and you, O Hanafis, have specified from this 'whoever kills in the house after entering' and 'whoever enters after cutting off his limbs' and you said: execution of retaliation is carried out on these two in the house. By analogy on the first two cases: i.e., killing after entering the house, and entering after cutting off limbs. And in it: that analogy on the criminal after entering the Kaaba is analogy with a difference, for he has violated the sanctity of the Kaaba so he has no security. As for the one who enters the Kaaba after killing, he seeks refuge in the Kaaba and honors it, so retaliation should not be executed on him, and he should have security. And its narrators are trustworthy. [Ishraq al-Absar 9]
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute regarding the second general term, 'man' in Quran 3:97, promising security to those who enter the Kaaba. The Shafi'i argues that the Hanafis have already specified two cases (killing inside after entry, and entering after mutilation) where they allow retaliation, so they should also specify the third case (entering after killing someone outside) by analogy on those two. The Hanafi response, as explained by al-Qamar, is that the analogy is invalid because the first two cases involve a violation of the Kaaba's sanctity (killing inside or entering with mutilation), whereas the third case involves one who honors the Kaaba by seeking refuge. Therefore, such a person retains security and retaliation is not executed inside. The passage also includes a hadith about slaughtering without mentioning Allah's name, which seems tangential but is part of the commentary's continuation.

Key Terms
من (man): A general term for 'whoever' in the verse.
قياس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): Analogy that is invalid because the two cases differ in the effective cause (illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis not apply retaliation to a murderer who enters the Kaaba after killing someone outside?
A) Because the Kaaba is a sanctuary for all criminals
B) Because such a person honors the Kaaba by seeking refuge, unlike those who violate its sanctity
C) Because the verse only applies to accidental killings
D) Because the solitary report forbids retaliation inside the Kaaba

Key Takeaway
The validity of an analogy depends on the presence of the same effective cause (illah); without it, the analogy is qiyas ma'a al-fariq and must be rejected.

The Hanafi Principle: 'Aamm is Qat'i — Rejecting Specification by Qiyas and Khabar al-Wahid
Refuting Shafi'i specification of two Quranic verses using qiyas and isolated hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'aamm is qat'i to identify why qiyas and khabar al-wahid cannot specify a general Quranic verse.

Core Idea
A general Quranic verse is definitive in its scope and cannot be limited by speculative proofs like qiyas or isolated hadith.

This passage defends a core Hanafi usul principle: a general text ('aamm) is binding on all its individuals until proven otherwise by equally strong evidence. The Shafi'i school considers 'aamm as zanni and allows specification by qiyas or ahad hadith. The author rebuts this using two Quranic verses, demonstrating that such specification would render the verses meaningless. By studying this refutation, you will understand the epistemological weight the Hanafi school places on textual generality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two verses and their general scope
Locate the two Quranic verses cited: 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (al-An'am 6:121) and 'Whoever enters it shall be safe' (Al Imran 3:97). Recognize that each contains a general term ('عام'): 'مِمَّا' and 'مَنْ' which cover all instances without restriction.
The general term 'مَنْ' includes any person entering the House.
2
Understand the Shafi'i specification proposal
The Shafi'i argues that the first verse is general for all cases where Allah's name is omitted, then specifies the intentional omission by qiyas on the forgetful (who is excused) and by the hadith 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he names or does not name.' For the second verse, he specifies the case of a killer entering after murder by qiyas on the killer inside and by the hadith 'The sanctuary does not give refuge to a sinner nor to one fleeing with blood.'
The Shafi'i view treats 'aamm as zanni, open to specification by zanni proofs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each specification
The author rejects both specifications. For the first verse, the qiyas is invalid (ma'a al-fariq) because the intentional person is not excused like the forgetful; the hadith is misinterpreted — it applies only when the name is omitted unintentionally. For the second verse, the hadith is weak (from a tyrant) and the qiyas fails because violating the sanctity of the House cannot be compared to taking refuge.
The Hanafi holds that the verses remain general, prohibiting all meat without basmalah (except idol sacrifices) and guaranteeing safety to all entrants (except those who violate the sanctity, as per other evidence).
4
Derive the usul principle from the refutation
The rejection is based on the principle that 'aamm is qat'i (definitive) in its generality. Only evidence that is also qat'i (another verse, mutawatir hadith, ijma) can specify it. Qiyas and khabar al-wahid are zanni and cannot override the definitive general meaning.
This principle is a hallmark of Hanafi usul, emphasizing textual certainty over analogical reasoning.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The dispute has direct fiqh consequences. Hanafi: Eating meat from an animal slaughtered by a Muslim who intentionally omits 'Bismillah' is unlawful. Shafi'i (according to one view): It is lawful because the slaughter is still valid. Similarly, a murderer who enters the Haram is safe according to the general verse, but Hanafi limits this by other evidence (e.g., the hadith about the sanctuary not protecting sinners, but only when authentically transmitted).
The thamarah shows that usul principles directly shape fatwa.

بيان حكم العام
مبحث العام إنه يجوز متروك التسمية ناسيًا، والآية محمولة على العامد فقط، قلنا: إن نخص العامد منه أيضًا بالقياس على الناسي، وبخبر الواحد وهو قوله علية: "المسلم يذبح على اسم الله سمى أو لم يسم"، " فلم يبق في الآية إلا ما كان مذبوحا بأسماء الأصنام. وتقرير الثاني: أن في قوله تعالى: وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِنًا كلمة "من" أيضًا عامة شاملة لمن دخل في البيت بعد قتل إنسان، أو بعد قطع أطرافه أو دخل في البيت ثم قتل فيه أحدًا، فينبغي أن يكون كل من هؤلاء آمنا وأنتم خصصتم من هذا "من قتل في البيت بعد الدخول،" و"من دخل فيه بعد قطع أطرافه ، وقلتم : إنه يقتص من هذين في البيت. قلنا: إن نخص الصورة الثالثة ،أيضا وهو: "من دخل في البيت بعد أن قتل إنسانًا"، فيقتص منه بالقياس على الصورتين الأوليين، وبخبر الواحد، وهو قوله علية : الحرم" لا يعيذ عاصيًا، ولا فارا بدم لم يبق تحت هذا العام إلا الآمن من عذاب النار، فأجاب المصنف له عن جانب أبي حنيفة حله بقوله: ولا يجوز تخصيص قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرَ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ﴾ وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كان آمنا بالقياس وخبر الواحد، أي لا يجوز تخصيص الشافعي له العامد عن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ﴾ بالقياس على الناسي، وقوله علي: "المسلم يذبح على اسم الله، سمى أو لم يسم"، وتخصيص الداخل في البيت بعد ما قتل عن قوله: ﴿وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِنًا﴾ بالقياس على القاتل بعد الدخول، وعلى الأطراف، وقوله علي: "الحرم لا يعيد عاصيا ولا فارا بدم".
لأنهما ليسا بمخصوصين تعليل لقوله : لا يجوز أي لأن هذين العامين ليسا بمخصوصين البقاء الحرم لا يعيد إلخ قصته أنه لما تخلف ابن الزبير وأشياعه عن بيعة يزيد أراد ترسيل البعث إلى مكة عمرو بن سعد من ولاة يزيد القتال مع ابن الزبير، فقال ابن شريح: إنه قال رسول الله : إن مكة حرم لا يصاد صيدها ولا يقطع شجرها، فقال: إن الحرم لا يعيذ عاصيًا ولا فارا بدم. كذا في صحيح البخاري، فهذا قوله: وهو ظالم بإرسال البعث إلى مكة، فلا اعتداد بقوله وقد جاء في بعض الروايات أن ابن شريح أنكر عليه من أن يكون هذا قوله عليه. (القمر) لم يبق إلخ والآية لم ترد لبيان الأمن من عذاب النار حتى يقال: إن هذا التخصيص صحيح بعض أفراد العام كما في الأول لا يكفى بقاء ما كان مذبوحا بأسماء الأصنام؛ لأن الآية وردت في المذبوحات التي ترك التسمية عليها وحرمتها من ذلك الوجه فقط، وذبائح الكفار حرمتها ليست من هذا الوجه؛ لأن الكافر الغير الكتابي لو ذكر التسمية فهو حرام أيضًا، كذا في الشافي شرح الشامي ، وإنما قلنا إن الآية لم ترد لبيان الأمن من عذاب النار، لأن الأمن منه يحصل لمن حج البيت إلا لمن دخله فقط، وأيضًا أورد تعالى بيان الحج بعدها بقوله: وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ (آل عمران: ۹۷) (السنبلي) وقوله : بالجر معطوف على المجرور في قوله بالقياس. (القمر) وتخصيص بالرفع معطوف على قوله: تخصيص الشافعي إلى آخره.(القمر)
أخرجه البخاري في "صحيحه" رقم ۱۷۳۵ ، باب إذا أهدى للمحرم حمارًا وحشيا حيا لم يقبل، ومسلم، رقم ١٣٥٤ ، باب تحريم مكة وصيدها وخلاها وشجرها ولقطتها إلا لمنشد على الدوام، والترمذي رقم: ۸۰۹ باب ما جاء في حرم مكة، وأحمد في مسنده ، رقم ۲۷۲۰۸، عن أبي شريح العدوي
Statement of the ruling of the general. [The Shafi'i says:] The verse is carried on the intentional [only]. We [Hanafis] say: We specify the intentional from it also by analogy to the forgetful, and by a single narration, namely his saying (peace be upon him): 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he names or does not name,' so nothing remains in the verse except what is slaughtered with the names of idols. And the explanation of the second [argument]: In the saying of Allah Most High: 'And whoever enters it shall be safe,' the word 'whoever' is also general, including one who enters the House after killing a person, or after cutting off his limbs, or enters the House and then kills someone therein. So every one of these should be safe, and you [Hanafis] have specified from this 'one who kills in the House after entering' and 'one who enters it after cutting off his limbs,' and you said: Retaliation is taken from these two in the House. We say: We also specify the third case, namely 'one who enters the House after killing a person,' and retaliation is taken from him by analogy to the first two cases, and by a single narration, namely his saying (peace be upon him): 'The sanctuary does not give refuge to a sinner nor to one fleeing with blood.' So nothing remains under this general [term] except the one safe from the punishment of the Fire. Then the author answered on behalf of Abu Hanifa with his saying: 'It is not permissible to specify the saying of Allah Most High: "And do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned" and "And whoever enters it shall be safe" by analogy and by a single narration.' That is, it is not permissible for al-Shafi'i to specify the intentional from the verse 'And do not eat...' by analogy to the forgetful, and his saying (peace be upon him): 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he names or does not name,' and to specify the one who enters the House after killing from the verse 'And whoever enters it shall be safe' by analogy to the killer after entering and to the limbs, and his saying (peace be upon him): 'The sanctuary does not give refuge to a sinner nor to one fleeing with blood.' Because they are not specifically delimited. This is the reason for his saying 'It is not permissible,' i.e., because these two general verses are not specifically delimited. The story of 'The sanctuary does not give refuge...' is that when Ibn al-Zubayr and his followers refused allegiance to Yazid, 'Amr ibn Sa'd from the governors of Yazid wanted to send an expedition to Mecca to fight Ibn al-Zubayr. Ibn Shurahbil said: Indeed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Mecca is a sanctuary: its game is not hunted, its trees are not cut.' He [Yazid] said: 'The sanctuary does not give refuge to a sinner nor to one fleeing with blood.' This is in Sahih al-Bukhari. So this was his saying, and he was unjust in sending the expedition to Mecca, so his saying is not considered. It has come in some narrations that Ibn Shurahbil denied that this was his saying (peace be upon him). As for 'nothing remains...' The verse [And do not eat] was not revealed to explain safety from the punishment of the Fire, such that one could say this specification is correct. As for the first, the survival of what was slaughtered with the names of idols is not sufficient, because the verse was revealed concerning slaughtered animals over which the name [of Allah] was omitted, and their prohibition is only from that aspect; the slaughtered animals of the disbelievers are prohibited not from this aspect, because if a non-bookish disbeliever mentions the name, it is also prohibited. And we only say that the verse was not revealed to explain safety from the punishment of the Fire, because safety from it is obtained for those who perform the Hajj to the House, not for those who only enter it. Also, Allah Most High mentioned the explanation of Hajj after it in His saying: 'And for Allah is the duty upon the people...' (Al Imran 97). And the word 'and' is genitive, coordinated with the genitive in 'by analogy'. (al-Qamar) 'And specification' is nominative, coordinated with 'the specification of al-Shafi'i' etc. (al-Qamar). It is narrated by al-Bukhari in his Sahih, no. 1735, chapter on... and Muslim no. 1354, etc.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i attempt to specify two general Quranic verses using qiyas (analogy) and khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith). The first verse is 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (al-An'am 121). The Shafi'i argues it is general for all cases where the name is omitted, but then specifies the intentional case by analogy to the forgetful (who is excused) and by a hadith stating that a Muslim's slaughter is valid whether he names Allah or not. The Hanafi response is that this specification is invalid for two reasons: (1) the analogy is faulty because the intentional person is not excused like the forgetful (qiyas ma'a al-fariq), and (2) the hadith is interpreted to mean that if a Muslim neither forgets nor intentionally omits the name, his slaughter is valid; it does not include intentional omission. Thus the verse remains general, prohibiting all meat where Allah's name is not mentioned, except that slaughtered for idols is already excluded because the verse is about the name being omitted, not about the slaughterer's belief. The second verse is 'And whoever enters it [the Kaaba] shall be safe' (Al Imran 97). The Shafi'i specifies those who kill after entering or enter after mutilation, using analogy and a hadith that the Haram does not give refuge to a sinner or one fleeing with blood. The Hanafi rejects this because the hadith is weak (from a tyrant ruler) and because the analogy is with the case of one who violates the sanctity of the House, which is different from one who takes refuge. The passage concludes that general texts remain general unless specified by equally strong evidence; qiyas and ahad reports are not sufficient. This is a key Hanafi usul principle: 'amm is qat'i (definitive) in its general scope and cannot be limited by zanni (speculative) proofs like qiyas or khabar al-wahid when they conflict with the apparent meaning.

Key Terms
العام (al-'aamm): A general term that covers all individuals of its category without restriction.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The limitation of a general term to some of its individuals by a separate evidence.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few chains, not reaching the level of tawatur.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul position defended in this passage, what is the ruling on specifying a general Quranic verse (such as 'Do not eat of that over which Allah's name has not been mentioned') using an analogy (qiyas) or a single-narrator hadith (khabar al-wahid)?
A) It is permissible because the verse is general and any valid proof can specify it.
B) It is not permissible because a general verse is qat'i and can only be specified by equally qat'i evidence.
C) It is permissible only if the analogy is based on a clear 'illa mentioned in the Quran.
D) It is permissible only if the hadith is narrated by two or more reliable narrators.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that 'aamm is qat'i means general Quranic texts cannot be specified by zanni proofs like qiyas and khabar al-wahid, preserving the certainty of divine law.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Specification of General Texts by Qiyas and Khabar al-Wahid
Refuting that general Quranic rulings can be specified by analogy or isolated reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies specification of a general text by qiyas or khabar al-wahid and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the examples from 6:121 and 3:97.

Core Idea
A general text ('amm) is qat'i and cannot be specified by zanni proofs like qiyas or khabar al-wahid.

This lesson tackles a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a general Quranic ruling be narrowed by analogy or an isolated hadith? The Hanafi position, presented here, insists on preserving the general scope until a definitive proof (Quran, mutawatir sunnah, ijma) specifies it. We will examine the reasoning behind this stance and the critique of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that the Hanafi school does not allow specification ('amm) by qiyas or khabar al-wahid. Understand the epistemic basis: the 'amm is qat'i, so only a qat'i proof can specify it.
2
Examine the Shafi'i examples
Look at the two verses quoted: 6:121 (forbidding meat without God's name) and 3:97 (security for those entering the Ka'bah). The Shafi'i argue that the forgetful person and the murderer are excluded from these general rulings by qiyas.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi reply: the forgetful person is not even included in the general prohibition because he is legally like a rememberer; the murderer after entry is not covered by the verse's security because the verse only protects those who enter while already free from liability. The hadith used (about the Haram not protecting sinners) is a specific historical statement, not a general legal principle.
Note the distinction between actual exclusion from the general vs. being outside its scope from the start.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: under Hanafi, the general ruling remains fully applied until a definitive specification comes; under Shafi'i, weaker proofs can narrow the application, e.g., permitting meat from a forgetful slaughterer.
5
Internalize the epistemic principle
Recognize that this disagreement stems from a deeper usul principle: the Hanafi classification of 'amm as qat'i al-dalalah vs. the Mutakallimin view that 'amm is zanni. This affects the hierarchy of proofs and the criteria for valid takhsis.

(القمر) لم يبق إلخ والآية لم ترد لبيان الأمن من عذاب النار حتى يقال: إن هذا التخصيص صحيح بعض أفراد العام كما في الأول لا يكفى بقاء ما كان مذبوحا بأسماء الأصنام؛ لأن الآية وردت في المذبوحات التي ترك التسمية عليها وحرمتها من ذلك الوجه فقط، وذبائح الكفار حرمتها ليست من هذا الوجه؛ لأن الكافر الغير الكتابي لو ذكر التسمية فهو حرام أيضًا، كذا في الشافي شرح الشامي، وإنما قلنا إن الآية لم ترد لبيان الأمن من عذاب النار، لأن الأمن منه يحصل لمن حج البيت إلا لمن دخله فقط، وأيضًا أورد تعالى بيان الحج بعدها بقوله: وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ... بيان حكم العام
أيها الشافعية
أولاً كما زعمتم حتى يخص ثانيا بالقياس، وخبر الواحد؛ لأن الناسي ليس بداخل في قوله تعالى: ﴿مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ﴾ أصلاً؛ إذ هو في معنى الذاكر فلم يخص من الآية حتى يقاس عليه العامد، وكذا الذي عليه قصاص في الطرف لم يخص من الآمن، إذ المراد بالآمر متروك التسمية عامدًا آمن الذات والأطراف، كأنها ليست... المال، الذات، بل من من... وكذا القاتل بعد الدخول أي ليس بداخل فيه؛ إذ معنى قوله: ﴿وَمَنْ دَخَلَهُ كَانَ آمِنًا﴾، من دخله بعد ما صار مباح الدم بردة، أو زنا، أو قصاص لا أنه باشر هذه الأمور بعد الدخول، فهو خارج عن مضمون الآية لا أنه القاتل بعد الدخول فيه مخصوص منها، لا يقال: إن ضمير "دخله" راجع إلى البيت، والمقصود بيان آمن الحرم؛ لأنا نقول: إن حكمها واحد بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا جَعَلْنَا حَرَمًا آمِنًا﴾ (العنكبوت: 67) إذ هو في معنى الذاكر إلخ يعني أن الناسي ذاكر حكمًا لقيام الملة الداعية إلى الذكر مقامه للعذر، فلا يكون متروك التسمية ناسيًا من أفراد ما لم يذكر اسم الله عليه، فلم يحضر إلخ، وما قال ابن الحاجب من أن الناسي مخصص اتفاقا، فهو صادر عن عدم الاطلاع على حقيقة مذهبنا وإلا لما حكم بالاتفاق. (القمر) في معنى: أي في حكمه؛ لقوله تعالى: لا تُؤَاخِذْنَا إِنْ نَسِينَا (البقرة: 286). (المحشي) لم يخص إلخ لأنه ليس بداخل في الأمن، إذ المراد إلخ. (القمر) كأنها ليست إلخ إشارة إلى أن الأطراف معززة، والمال ذليل، فلا مناسبة بين الأطراف والمال، إلا أن الأطراف كالمال في نظر الشارع لا كالأنفس لسهولة أمر الأطراف، بخلاف الأنفس فإن أمرها خطير. (القمر) كأنها ليست إلخ إنما قال: لفظ "كأن"؛ لأن نفي الذات عن الأجزاء حقيقة متعسر، ووجه تشبيه الأطراف بالمال أن الأطراف خلقت وقاية للنفس كما أن المال مخلوق لوقايتها، ولذا قالوا الأطراف يسلك بها مسلك الأموال. (السنبلي) ومن دخله إلخ فهو آمن لا يتعرض له لكنه يلجأ إلى الخروج بأن لا يطعم ولا يسقى حتى يخرج. (القمر) لا يقال إلخ اعتراض حاصله : أن الضمير المنصوب في "ومن دخله" راجع إلى البيت لسبق ذكره لا إلى الحرم، لعدم ذكره، فإثبات الأمن لمن قتل، ثم دخل في الحرم بهذه الآية مشكل. (القمر) لأنا نقول إن إلخ جواب توضيحه أن الضمير المنصوب وإن كان راجعا إلى البيت إلا أن الحرم أخذ حكم البيت و هو الأمن بنص آخر، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّا جَعَلْنَا حَرَمًا آمِنًا﴾ (العنكبوت:67) أي أو لم يعلموا أنا جعلنا بلدهم مكة حرما آمنا كذا في الجلالين، فلا فصل حينئذ بين البيت وحرمه في الأمن بل كل منهما محل الأمن. (القمر)
Section on the General. Explanation of the ruling of the general, and it is his statement, peace be upon him: 'The sanctuary does not protect a sinner, nor a fugitive for blood.' ... nothing remained under this general except the one safe from the torment of the Fire. So the author answered regarding the side of Abu Hanifa by his statement: 'It is not permissible to specify the statement of Allah Most High: "And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned" (al-An'am 6:121) and "And whoever enters it is secure" (Aal 'Imran 3:97) by analogy and isolated report.' That is, it is not permissible for al-Shafi'i to specify the intentional [sinner] from the statement of Allah Most High: "And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned" by analogy to the forgetful person, and his statement, peace be upon him: 'The Muslim slaughters in the name of Allah, whether he names or does not name,' and to specify the one who enters the House after having killed from the statement: "And whoever enters it is secure" by analogy to the one who kills after entering, and to the limbs, and his statement, peace be upon him: 'The sanctuary does not protect a sinner nor a fugitive for blood.' Because these two are not specified, a justification for his statement: 'it is not permissible' — i.e., because these two general texts are not specified...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul al-fiqh dispute. The text argues against the Shafi'i position that a general ('amm) Quranic ruling can be specified (takhsis) by qiyas (analogy) or khabar al-wahid (isolated hadith). The author (commentator on Noorul Anwaar) refutes this using two examples. First, Surah al-An'am 6:121 forbids eating meat upon which Allah's name was not mentioned. The Shafi'i argue that the forgetful person is excluded from this general prohibition by qiyas — since he is excused, the intentional omission is the real target. The Hanafi response: the forgetful person is not even within the scope of the 'amm because he is legally like a rememberer (dhakir) due to the latent intention; thus there is no specification needed. Second, Surah Aal 'Imran 3:97 declares that whoever enters the Ka'bah is secure. The Shafi'i argue that a murderer who enters after killing is excluded by qiyas. The Hanafi reply: the verse only applies to someone who enters while already being secure in his person; a murderer who becomes liable to qisas after the act is not within the 'amm at all. Furthermore, the hadith about the Haram not protecting sinners is from a specific historical context (Ibn al-Zubayr's rebellion) and was not intended as a universal legal principle. The commentary also clarifies that the general texts remain intact and are not subject to specification by weak proofs like qiyas or ahad hadith. The Hanafi school upholds the integrity of the 'amm until it is specified by a text of equal or higher authority.

Key Terms
العام (al-'amm): A word that refers to all individuals or items of its kind without restriction.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The process of excluding some individuals from a general ruling by a specific proof.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illah).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by a single chain of narrators, not reaching mutawatir level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a general Quranic verse be specified by qiyas (analogy)?
A) Yes, because qiyas is a valid source of Islamic law.
B) No, because qiyas cannot specify a general text that is qat'i.
C) Yes, if the qiyas is based on a clear 'illah.
D) No, because specification is only by mutawatir texts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a definitive proof (qat'i) to specify a general text; qiyas and khabar al-wahid are insufficient due to their zanni nature.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Authoritativeness of 'Aam (General) Until Specification
Defends Hanafi position on 'aam's authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that a general text ('aam) remains authoritative (hujjah) before specification, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the forgetful person and the killer in the sanctuary.

Core Idea
A general text is proof (hujjah) on all its instances until explicit specification — analogy and isolated reports cannot narrow its scope before specification.

The Hanafi school holds that a general ('aam) text is definitive (qat'i) in its scope and remains binding until a clear proof specifies it. The Shafi'is, however, consider general texts as probable (zanni) and open to qualification by qiyas and khabar wahid even before specification. This passage defends the Hanafi view through two Quranic examples, refuting the Shafi'i claim of consensus on the forgetful person's exclusion.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the core issue: Is a general text authoritative before specification? Hanafis say yes, Shafi'is say it can be limited by qiyas and khabar wahid without explicit specification.
2
Analyze the first example (al-An'am 121)
Understand the Shafi'i claim that the forgetful person is excluded by consensus and qiyas includes the intentional. Then examine the Hanafi response that the forgetful person was never an individual of the general term because he is in the meaning of the remembrancer.
Key: The forgetful person is not an individual originally, so no specification occurred.
3
Analyze the second example (Al 'Imran 97)
Understand the Shafi'i claim that the killer after entering is specified out. Then examine the Hanafi response that the killer was never included because the security applies only before entering.
The killer's state before entry contradicts the condition of security.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: For Hanafis, a general verse can be cited as proof immediately; for Shafi'is, it is treated as probable and open to qualification before use.
5
Evaluate the strength of the Hanafi response
Consider the logic: The Hanafi position preserves the literal scope until a clear proof of specification arrives, while the Shafi'i approach risks premature narrowing.
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that an individual must be within the general's scope to be specified.

Section on the General (al-‘Aam). Statement of the ruling of the general. O you Shafi’is! Firstly, as you claim, it is specified only secondly by analogical deduction (qiyas) and isolated report (khabar al-wahid); because the forgetful person is not included in His saying: 'from that over which Allah’s name is not taken' originally; because he is in the meaning of the one who remembers, so he was not excluded from the verse so that the intentional one could be analogized to him. Similarly, the one who has retaliation due on him for a limb is not excluded from the secure one, because what is meant by the secure one is the one whose self and limbs are secure, as if they are not like property. And similarly, the killer after entering [the sanctuary]—i.e., he is not included in it; because the meaning of His saying: 'And whoever enters it is secure' is: whoever enters it after he has become permissible to kill due to apostasy, or adultery, or retaliation—not that he commits these actions after entering. So he is outside the purport of the verse, not that the killer after entering is specified from it. It cannot be said: The accusative pronoun in 'enters it' refers to the House, and the intent is to state the security of the sanctuary; because we say: Their ruling is one, by the evidence of His saying: 'Do they not see that We made a sanctuary secure.' (al-‘Ankabut: 67) [The commentary continues with explanations from al-Qamar, al-Sanbali, etc.]
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute with the Shafi‘i school regarding the authority of general texts (‘aam). The Hanafi position is that a general text remains authoritative (hujjah) until it is specified by a valid proof. The Shafi‘is claim that a general text can be specified by qiyas and khabar al-wahid even before it is specified, which the Hanafis reject. The author provides two examples: (1) The verse prohibiting consumption of meat over which Allah’s name is not taken (al-An‘am: 121). The Shafi‘is argue that the forgetful person (al-nasi) is excluded from this general prohibition by consensus, and then they use qiyas to include the intentional person. The Hanafis respond that the forgetful person is not included in the verse originally because he is in the 'meaning' of the one who remembers (i.e., he has the excuse of forgetfulness), so there is no need for specification. Hence, the general remains as it is. (2) The verse stating that whoever enters the House (or sanctuary) is secure (Al ‘Imran: 97). The Shafi‘is claim that a killer who enters after committing murder is excluded by specification. The Hanafis argue that such a person was never included in the security because the security applies to one whose blood was originally inviolable, not to one who became permissible to kill before entering. The author also refutes the objection that the pronoun in 'enters it' refers to the House, not the sanctuary, by citing another verse that establishes the sanctuary shares the same ruling of security. The passage is from the sharh of Nur al-Anwar, with glosses from al-Qamar and al-Sanbali expanding on the reasoning.

Key Terms
عام (‘aam): A word that encompasses all its individuals without restriction.
تخصيص (takhsis): Limiting a general term to some of its individuals by an independent connected statement.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the forgetful person not considered an individual of the general prohibition in the verse 'Do not eat of that over which Allah's name is not taken'?
A) Because the forgetful person is excluded by consensus.
B) Because the forgetful person is in the meaning of the one who remembers, due to the excuse of forgetfulness.
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because qiyas removes the forgetful person from the general.

Key Takeaway
A general text ('aam) is a binding proof (hujjah) on all its individuals until a clear specification (takhsis) is established; being in the meaning of a specified exception does not constitute takhsis.

The Specified General: Status and Definition
Definition and ruling of the specified general.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the ruling of a specified general after takhsis and IDENTIFY the conditions for valid takhsis in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A specified general is zanni but still binding.

In the previous lesson, we learned about the general ('aam) and its definitive authority before any specification. Now we examine what happens when a general is limited by a specifier (mukhassis). The key question: does it retain its original certainty? The Hanafi school holds that it does not, but it remains a binding proof for action. This lesson unpacks the definition of the specified general and the technical conditions for valid takhsis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and find the sentence: 'fain lahiqahu khusus...'. State what happens to the general when specification occurs.
Do not skip the word 'majhool' – unknown specifier also has the same effect.
2
Understand the Epistemological Shift
Explain why the general loses its qat'i status and becomes zanni. The passage compares it to other zanni proofs like khabar wahid and qiyas.
This does not mean it becomes weak; it still must be acted upon.
3
Define Takhsis
Extract the definition: 'qasr al-'aam 'ala ba'di musammayatihi bikalaamin mustaqillin mawsulin'. Identify the three conditions: must be a statement, independent, and connected.
If it is not a statement (e.g., reason, custom), it is not technically takhsis but can still restrict meaning.
4
Distinguish Takhsis from Naskh
The commentary notes that the specifier must be connected (mawsul). If it is separate and later, it becomes naskh, not takhsis. Understand the difference.
Some scholars debated whether a second occurrence of specification is naskh or takhsis.

ثم إن المصنف محله لما فرغ عن بيان العام الغير المخصوص شرع في بيان العام المخصوص، وأورد فيه ثلاثة ،مذاهب وبين كل مذهب بدليل وشبهه بمسألة فقهية، فقال: فإن لحقه خصوص معلوم أو مجهول لا يبقى قطعيًا لكنه لا يسقط الاحتجاج به أي إن لحق هذا العام الذي كان قطعيًا مخصص معلوم المراد أو مجهول المراد، فالمختار أنه لا تبقى قطعية، ولكن يجب العمل به، كما شأن سائر الدلائل الظنية من خبر الواحد والقياس، والتخصيص في الاصطلاح هو قصر العام على بعض مسمياته بكلام مستقل موصول، فإن لم يكن كلاما بأن كان عقلاً أو حسا، أو عادة، أو نحوه لم يكن تخصيصا اصطلاحا،

(القمر)
أو نحوه ككون بعض الأفراد ناقصاً أو زائدا ، أما العقل فكقولنا: "خالق كل شيء" فإنه عام، والعقل حاكم بأن المراد من كل شيء ما سوى الله تعالى، وقيل: إن المراد من الشيء في قوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ خَالِقُ كُلِّ (الأنعام: ۱۰۲) =
Section on the General (al-‘Aam). Statement of the Specified General. Then, when the author (the matn) finished the statement of the general that is not specified, he began the statement of the specified general, and presented three schools (madhhabs), explaining each school with evidence and its likeness in a legal issue. He said: 'If a specification (khusus) known or unknown follows it, it does not remain definitive (qat‘i), but it does not cease to be used as proof.' That is, if this general that was definitive is overtaken by a specifier whose intended meaning is known or unknown, the chosen position is that it does not remain definitive, but it must be acted upon, like other speculative proofs such as isolated reports and analogical deduction. Specification in terminology is: restricting the general to some of its individuals by an independent connected statement. If it is not a statement, such as if it is reason, sense, custom, or the like, it is not considered specification in terminology. [Commentary follows from al-Qamar and al-Sanbali on the term 'khusus' meaning the specifier, etc.]
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from a sharh of Nur al-Anwar defines the specified general ('aam al-makhsoos). After discussing the unspecific general, the author now deals with the case when a general text has been specified. The main ruling: The specified general loses its definitive (qat‘i) status and becomes probable (zanni), but it remains authoritative and must be acted upon. The author mentions three madhhabs on this issue (though not detailed here). Then he provides a technical definition of takhsis: restricting the general to some individuals by an independent connected statement. If the specifier is not a statement (e.g., reason, sense, custom), it is not called takhsis in terminology; but such factors can also specify. The commentary by al-Qamar clarifies that 'khusus' in the phrase 'fain lahiqahu khusus' means 'al-mukhassis' (the specifier), not the act of specification. It also explains that the specifier must be 'connected' (mawsul) to count as takhsis; if it is separate and later, it becomes naskh (abrogation), not takhsis. There is a difference of opinion among scholars whether the second instance of takhsis is actually naskh.

Key Terms
عام مخصوص (‘aam makhsoos): A general term that has been limited in its application by a specifier, losing its definitiveness but remaining binding.
تخصيص (takhsis): Restricting a general term to some of its individuals by an independent connected statement.
قطعي (qat‘i): Definitive certainty, a ruling that is beyond doubt.
ظني (zanni): Probable, speculative; not definitive but still authoritative for action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a general text ('aam) is specified by a connected independent statement, what is its legal status according to the Hanafi school?
A) It becomes completely invalid and cannot be used as proof.
B) It remains definitive (qat‘i) and binding.
C) It becomes speculative (zanni) but remains binding and authoritative.
D) It is considered abrogated (mansukh).

Key Takeaway
The specified general ('aam makhsoos) is a proof of speculative certainty (zanni) that must be acted upon, and it is valid only when the specifier is a connected independent statement; otherwise it may be naskh.

The Hanafi Condition of Connection in Specification
Explaining specification types and Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on sequential specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi condition that a specifier must be connected to the general, and explain why a disconnected specifier is considered naskh rather than takhsis, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Connection makes it takhsis; disconnection makes it naskh.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of specification (takhsis) includes a critical condition: the specifier must be connected to the general term. This seemingly technical point has major implications for how we understand sequential restrictions of general texts. A later, disconnected specifier is not a second specification at all—it is abrogation (naskh). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning and the resulting dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Hanafi definition of takhsis
The text defines takhsis as 'restricting the general to some of its individuals by an independent connected speech.' Note the two key conditions: independent speech and connection.
Non-independent specifiers (ghayah, shart, etc.) are also valid as long as they are connected.
2
Distinguish connected vs disconnected specifiers
A specifier is connected (mawsul) if it appears in the same context without temporal gap. Disconnected (mutarakhin) means it appears later, separately. The Hanafi ruling: disconnected specifiers are not takhsis but naskh.
The text emphasizes 'موصول' (connected) as essential.
3
Understand the Shafi'i alternative
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that connection is not a condition; any specifier that restricts the general is takhsis, regardless of temporal separation. The second specification is still valid as takhsis.
The Shafi'i definition focuses solely on restricting the scope of the general.
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis treat a later disconnected specifier as naskh, requiring conditions for abrogation (like impossibility of simultaneous application). Shafi'is treat it as takhsis, which has no such conditions, making interpretation more flexible.
Example: a general verse followed by a later specific verse—Hanafis must check if the later verse can be considered abrogating; Shafi'is simply take it as specification.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi response argues that if a specifier is disconnected, the original general must have been intended for all individuals; the later restriction lifts part of that intent, which is the essence of naskh. The term 'takhsis' is sometimes used loosely for such cases, but technically it is naskh.
The text notes that Hanafis themselves sometimes use 'takhsis' loosely, e.g., 'the Book was specified by the Sunnah,' but this is metaphorical.
