مبحث العام

بيان العام المخصوص

ثم إن المصنف لما فرغ عن بيان العام الغير المخصوص شرع في بيان العام المخصوص، وأورد فيه ثلاثة مذاهب وبين كل مذهب بدليل وشبهه بمسألة فقهية، فقال: فإن لحقه خصوص معلوم أو مجهول لا يبقى قطعيًا لكنه لا يسقط الاحتجاج به أي إن لحق هذا العام الذي كان قطعيًا مخصص معلوم المراد أو مجهول المراد، فالمختار أنه لا تبقى قطعية، ولكن يجب العمل به، كما شأن سائر الدلائل الظنية من خبر الواحد والقياس، والتخصيص في الاصطلاح هو قصر العام على بعض مسمياته بكلام مستقل موصول، فإن لم يكن كلاما بأن كان عقلاً أو حسا، أو عادة، أو نحوه لم يكن تخصيصا اصطلاحا،

هو
المخصص

فإن لحقه إلخ: هذا بظاهره يدل على أن الخصوص يكون لاحقًا متأخرا، وهذا خلاف التحقيق، فإن التخصيص يكون بالموصول، فمعنى الكلام حينئذ فإن ظهر دليل الخصوص إلخ، فالخصوص ههنا بمعنى المخصص، أو المضاف محذوف أي دليل الخصوص. (القمر) مخصص معلوم المراد الخ: هذا دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن التخصيص معلوم في المجهول أيضًا، فكيف يستقيم قول الماتن: أو مجهول، وخلاصة الدفع أن الخصوص مصدر بمعنى الفاعل أي خاص معلوم المراد أو مجهوله، أو بمعنى المفعول أي مخصوص معلوم المراد أو مجهوله، أو على حقيقته، والمضاف محذوف أي دليل خصوص معلوم المراد أو مجهوله والشارح أخذ الخصوص بمعنى المخصص، وهو أيضًا اسم الفاعل. (السنبلي) معلوم المراد إلخ إيماء إلى دفع ما يتوهم من أن دليل الخصوص يكون معلوما، فلا وجه لترديده بين المعلوم والمجهول كما هو في المتن . (القمر) بكلام مستقل أي بكلام يفيد حكما بانفراده، وغير المستقل ما لا يفيد حكمًا لو ذكر منفردًا، كالغاية والصفة وغيرهما . (القمر) موصول فيه إيماء إلى أن التخصيص في المرة الثانية ليس بتخصيص اصطلاحا بل هو نسخ، لكونه متراخيا كذا أفاد بحر العلوم ، وقال بعض الشراح: إن المقارنة شرط للمخصص أول مرة، وليس داخلا في ماهيته فحينئذٍ كان التخصيص في المرة الثانية تخصيصا اصطلاحًا. (القمر)

أو نحوه ككون بعض الأفراد ناقصاً أو زائدا ، أما العقل فكقولنا: "خالق كل شيء" فإنه عام، والعقل حاكم بأن المراد من كل شيء ما سوى الله تعالى، وقيل: إن المراد من الشيء في قوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ خَالِقُ كُلِّ (الأنعام: ١٠٢) = المخلوق بقرينة إضافة الخالق إليه فلا يتناوله، فكيف يكون مخصوصا بالعقل تأمل ومن هذا القبيل خروج الصبيان والمجانين من الأحكام التكليفية فإنه بالعقل وأما الحس نحو أوتيت من كل شيء، "وأما العادة فنحو: لا يأكل رأسًا فيقع على المتعارف لا على رأس الجراد، وأما كون بعض الأفراد ناقصا نحو: كل مملوك لي فهو حر" فلا يقع على المكاتب لنقصان الملك فيه فإنه مملوك رقبة لا يدًا، وأما كون بعض الأفراد زائدا فنحو: الحلف بأن لا يأكل فاكهة ولا نية له، فإنه لا يقع على الرطب، فإنه وإن كان فاكهة عرفًا ولغة، إلا أن فيه معنى زائدا على التفكه أي التلذذ والتنعم وهو الغذائية، وقوام البدن . (القمر)

ولم يصر أي العام ظنيًا، وهذا إذا كان المخصص العقل، فإن ما حكم العقل بخروجه يخرج ويبقى الدلالة قطعية على الباقي كما كانت وأما إذا كان المخصص الحس أو العادة، أو نحوهما، فالظاهر أن لا يبقى قطعيًا، لاختلاف العادات، وخفاء الزيادة والنقصان، وعدم اطلاع الحس على تفاصيل الأشياء، اللهم إلا أن يعلم القدر المخصوص قطعًا كذا في "التلويح". (القمر)

وكذا إلخ: أي لا يكون تخصيصا اصطلاحًا إن لم يكن أي المخصص مستقلاً، بل كان التخصيص بغاية إلخ، أما الغاية إلخ، فنحو: ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيل (البقرة: ١٨٧) وأما الشرط فنحو: "أنت طالق إن دخلت الدار" فقصر صدر الكلام على بعض التقادير ، وأما الاستثناء فنحو: جاء في القوم إلا زيدا، وأما الصفة فنحو: "في الإبل السائمة "زكاة، ثم اعلم أنه ليس غير المستقل منحصراً في هذه الأربعة، بل له قسم خامس أيضًا، وهو بدل البعض نحو : جاءني القوم أكثرهم. (القمر) بل نسخا ففي التخصيص إرادة البعض من العام من أول الأمر، وفي النسخ أريد الكل من العام، ثم رفع حكم البعض. (القمر)

مطلقًا أي أعم من أن يكون المستقل أو بغيره موصولاً أو غير موصول.(القمر)

وكثيرا ما يطلق إلخ كما يقال خص الكتاب بالسنة، وخص بعض الآيات بالبعض مع التراخي. عندنا: فلا وجه للقول السابق لا يسمى تخصيصا بل نسخا.(المحشي)

سيجيء
وسيجيء
Section on the general specified: When a general is followed by a specification known or unknown, it does not remain qat'i but does not lose its validity as a proof. Specification in terminology is restricting the general to some of its individuals by an independent connected speech. If it is not speech but rather intellect, sense, custom, or the like, it is not specification in terminology. Then it discusses the conditions for the specifier and the dispute: According to the Hanafis, if the specifier is not independent but rather a ghayah, shart, istithna, or sifat, it is still specification. If it is not connected but rather separated, it is not specification but abrogation. According to al-Shafi'i, all of that is called specification. Examples are given.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar explains the nature of a general that has been specified (al-‘amm al-makhsus). The author first states that when a general is followed by a specification—whether the meaning of the specifier is known or unknown—the general loses its qat’i (definitive) status and becomes zanni (speculative), yet it remains a valid proof (hujjah) to be acted upon, like other zanni evidences such as khabar al-wahid and qiyas. This ruling applies to the Hanafi school.

The passage then defines ‘specification’ (takhsis) in Hanafi usul: it is the restriction of a general term to some of its individuals by an independent, connected speech. If the specifier is not speech—like intellect, sense perception, custom, or deficiency/excess in some individuals—it is not considered specification in the technical sense. For example, the Quranic verse 'He is the Creator of everything' is general, but intellect excludes Allah Himself from 'everything.' Similarly, the exclusion of children and the insane from taklifi rulings is by intellect.

The text elaborates that if the specifier is independent (like a separate statement) and connected, it is takhsis. If it is non-independent (like a ghayah, shart, istithna, or sifat) but still connected, it is also takhsis. However, if the specifier is disconnected (mutarakhin), then according to the Hanafis it is not takhsis but naskh (abrogation). The reason is that in takhsis, the general was intended from the beginning to apply only to some individuals, whereas in naskh, the general originally applied to all, then the ruling for some was lifted.

A key dispute arises: Imam al-Shafi’i holds that even a disconnected specifier is called takhsis, and sequential specifications are permissible. The Hanafis counter that such usage is merely metaphorical; in reality, a second specification is naskh. The text notes that Hanafis themselves sometimes use 'takhsis' loosely for disconnected specifications, as in 'the Book was specified by the Sunnah,' but technically it is naskh.

This passage is crucial for understanding how Hanafis distinguish between abrogation and specification, a distinction that has significant fiqh implications for the interpretation of texts.

Key Terms
العام المخصوص (al-‘āmm al-makhṣūṣ): A general term that has been restricted by a specifier, losing its definitive indication but remaining a valid proof.
التخصيص (al-takhṣīṣ): Restricting a general term to some of its individuals by an independent, connected speech.
المستقل (al-mustaqill): A specifier that is an independent speech that conveys a ruling by itself (e.g., a separate verse).
الموصول (al-mawṣūl): Connected to the general in the same context, without temporal separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a general text is first specified by a connected specifier, and then a later disconnected specifier restricts it further, what is the second restriction called?
A) Takhsis (specification)
B) Naskh (abrogation)
C) Ta'yin (specification of an ambiguous term)
D) Taqyid (restriction of an absolute term)

Key Takeaway
Connection (wasl) is the essential condition that distinguishes specification from abrogation in Hanafi usul; a disconnected second specifier is naskh, not takhsis.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Effect of Different Types of Takhṣīṣ on the Qaṭ‘iyyah of al-‘Āmm
Explaining how specification by intellect, sense, custom, etc. affects categorical nature of general terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the type of mukhaṣṣiṣ specified in a usul text and apply the Hanafi rule to determine whether the general term remains qaṭ‘ī or becomes ẓannī.

Core Idea
Intellectual specification preserves the general's certainty; custom and sense render it probable.

This passage from our usul text examines how different types of specification (takhṣīṣ) affect the epistemic status of a general term (al-‘āmm). The Hanafi school distinguishes between independent mukhaṣṣiṣ, such as intellect, which leaves the general qaṭ‘ī, and non-independent or customary specifications, which reduce it to ẓannī. The text also contrasts the Hanafi view with al-Shāfi‘ī’s broader definition of takhṣīṣ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term
Locate the lafẓ ‘āmm in the given usul passage. It is the word that encompasses all individuals of its category.
In the passage, examples include 'al-bay‘' (trade), 'kullu mamlūk' (every slave), 'ra’s' (head), 'fākihat' (fruit).
2
Identify the type of mukhaṣṣiṣ
Determine the evidence specifying the general: is it from intellect, sense, custom, or a textual connector (ghāya, shart, istithnā’, ṣifa, or delayed)?
Intellect-based: minors and insane from obligations; sense-based: 'ūtīt min kulli shay’'. Custom: 'lā ya’kulu ra’s'. Deficiency: mukātab. Excess: ripe dates.
3
Classify the mukhaṣṣiṣ as independent or non-independent
Independent mukhassis (intellect) are those that do not rely on language; non-independent include textual connectors and delayed specifications.
Hanafis treat delayed specification as naskh, not takhṣīṣ.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule on epistemic effect
For independent intellect, the general remains qaṭ‘ī. For sense/custom, it becomes ẓannī unless the specified portion is known with certainty. For textual connectors and delayed, the rule shifts to naskh.
The passage states: 'إذا كان المخصص العقل ... ويبقى الدلالة قطعية; فإن المخصص الحس أو العادة ... فالظاهر أن لا يبقى قطعيًا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يصر ظنيًا، وكذا إن لم يكن مستقلاً، بل كان بغاية أو شرط، أو استثناء، أو صفة تفاصيلها وكذا إن لم يكن موصولاً، بل كان متراخيا لا تخصيصا، بل نسخا على يسمى ما سيجيء، هكذا قالوا، وعند الشافعي له كل ذلك يسمى تخصيصا؛ لأنه عنده هو قصر التخصيص العام على بعض المسميات مطلقا، وكثيرًا ما يطلق التخصيص على التراخي مجازا عندنا أيضا. ونظير الخصوص المعلوم والمجهول قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللَّهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا فإن البيع لفظ عام؛ = (البقرة: ٢٧٥) المخلوق بقرينة إضافة الخالق إليه فلا يتناوله، فكيف يكون مخصوصا بالعقل تأمل ومن هذا القبيل خروج الصبيان والمجانين من الأحكام التكليفية فإنه بالعقل وأما الحس نحو أوتيت من كل شيء، "وأما العادة فنحو: لا يأكل رأسًا فيقع على المتعارف لا على رأس الجراد، وأما كون بعض الأفراد ناقصا نحو: كل مملوك لي فهو حر" فلا يقع على المكاتب لنقصان الملك فيه فإنه مملوك رقبة لا يدًا، وأما كون بعض الأفراد زائدا فنحو: الحلف بأن لا يأكل فاكهة ولا نية له، فإنه لا يقع على الرطب، فإنه وإن كان فاكهة عرفًا ولغة، إلا أن فيه معنى زائدا على التفكه أي التلذذ والتنعم وهو الغذائية، وقوام البدن . (القمر) ولم يصر أي العام ظنيًا، وهذا إذا كان المخصص العقل، فإن ما حكم العقل بخروجه يخرج ويبقى الدلالة قطعية على الباقي كما كانت وأما إذا كان المخصص الحس أو العادة، أو نحوهما، فالظاهر أن لا يبقى قطعيًا، لاختلاف العادات، وخفاء الزيادة والنقصان، وعدم اطلاع الحس على تفاصيل الأشياء، اللهم إلا أن يعلم القدر المخصوص قطعًا كذا في "التلويح". (القمر)
And it [the general] does not become zanni; similarly if it [the mukhaṣṣiṣ] is not independent but rather by a ghāya, or a shart, or an istithnā', or a ṣifa, with their details; and similarly if it is not connected [to the general] but is delayed, it is not called takhṣīṣ but rather naskh, as will come. Thus they said. And according to al-Shāfi‘ī, all of that is called takhṣīṣ because, according to him, it is restricting the general to some of its meanings absolutely. And often takhṣīṣ is applied metaphorically to the delayed [takhṣīṣ] according to us as well. And an example of the known and unknown specific [meaning] is the saying of the Exalted: 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden ribā' [al-Baqara 2:275], for 'trade' is a general word; (al-Baqara: 275) [it is] created by the indication of attributing the Creator to it, so it does not include Him. How then can it be specified by the intellect? Ponder. And of this category is the exclusion of minors and the insane from obligatory rulings, for that is by intellect. As for sense, e.g., 'you were given of everything'; and as for custom, e.g., 'he does not eat a head'— it applies to what is customary, not to the head of a locust. And as for some individuals being deficient, e.g., 'every slave of mine is free'— it does not apply to a mukātab due to the deficiency of ownership in him, for he is a slave of the neck but not of the hand. And as for some individuals being excessive, e.g., one swears not to eat fruit without intention; it does not apply to ripe dates, for, although they are fruit according to custom and language, there is in them an additional meaning beyond enjoyment, i.e., delight and pleasure, which is nourishment and the sustenance of the body. (al-Qamar) And it [the general] does not become zanni— this is when the mukhaṣṣiṣ is the intellect, for what the intellect rules to be excluded is excluded, and the indication remains qaṭ‘ī concerning the remainder as before. But if the mukhaṣṣiṣ is sense or custom or the like, then apparently it does not remain qaṭ‘ī, due to the variation of customs, the hiddenness of increase and decrease, and the lack of sense’s knowledge of the details of things, unless the specified amount is known with certainty. Thus in 'al-Talwīḥ'. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of how different types of specification (takhṣīṣ) affect the categorical (qaṭ‘ī) or probable (ẓannī) nature of a general term (al-‘āmm). The author begins by stating that the general does not become ẓannī when specified by an independent mukhassis (e.g., intellect). However, when the mukhassis is non-independent—such as a limiting clause (ghāya), condition (shart), exception (istithnā’), or adjective (ṣifa)—or when it is delayed, the Hanafis do not consider it technical takhṣīṣ but rather naskh (abrogation), whereas al-Shāfi‘ī considers it takhṣīṣ. The author then provides examples: the verse 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden ribā' is a general term (trade) that is specified by the context of attributing to God, showing that trade does not include God’s actions. Similarly, the exclusion of minors and insane from obligations is specification by intellect. Examples of specification by custom include the phrase 'he does not eat a head,' which customarily refers to a common head, not a locust’s head. Specification by deficiency is illustrated by a slave who is a mukātab (indentured servant) not being included in 'every slave of mine is free' due to incomplete ownership. Specification by excess is shown in a vow not to eat fruit, where ripe dates are excluded because they have an additional nutritive quality beyond mere fruit. The second paragraph clarifies that when the mukhassis is intellect, the general remains qaṭ‘ī for the remaining individuals. But if the mukhassis is sense or custom, the general becomes ẓannī because customs vary and sensory details are uncertain, unless the specified portion is known with certainty. This is based on the famous Hanafi usul work 'al-Talwīḥ'.

Key Terms
العام (al-‘āmm): A verbal utterance that encompasses all the individuals of its category without restriction.
المخصص (al-mukhaṣṣiṣ): The evidence that restricts a general ruling to some of its individuals, excluding others.
ظني (ẓannī): Probable; a ruling that is based on speculation rather than certainty.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; the removal of a legal ruling by a later revealed text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of specification preserves the qaṭ‘iyyah of a general term?
A) Specification by custom
B) Specification by sense
C) Specification by intellect
D) Specification by deficiency (nuqṣān)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intellectual specification does not affect the certainty of a general term, while custom and sense render it probable unless the specified portion is known with certainty.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Status of al-‘Amm al-Makhsoos and the ‘Illah of Riba
Explaining the status of a specified general and the derivation of the ‘illah of riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a specified general remains qat‘i for its remaining instances but is open to ta‘lil, and apply this by comparing the three major views on the ‘illah of riba.

Core Idea
The specified general stays definitive for its content but allows rational extension through ta‘lil.

This lesson examines a sophisticated Hanafi usul principle: how a general text retains its authority after being partially specified. The Quranic prohibition of riba serves as a classic example, leading to different opinions on the effective cause of riba. You will see how the Hanafi school balances textual certainty with the need for analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem of the specified general
The verse 'and Allah prohibited riba' (2:275) is general. The Prophet ﷺ specified riba in six commodities. This raises the question: does the general verse still have authority for other items?
The word 'riba' in the verse is a general term with the lam of genus.
2
Identify three major usul positions
Some scholars (second madhhab) treat specification like exception, voiding the general entirely. Others (third madhhab) treat it like abrogation, keeping the general frozen. The Hanafis take a middle path.
The text refers to these as 'madhhab thani' and 'madhhab thalith'.
3
Grasp the Hanafi solution: resemblance to exception and naskh
The specified general resembles exception in that the excluded items never fell under the general, so the general remains qat‘i for the rest. It also resembles abrogation in that the specifying evidence is independent, so the general becomes open to ta‘lil.
This dual resemblance is the key to the Hanafi position.
4
Apply ta‘lil to derive the ‘illah of riba
Because the general is open to ta‘lil, the Companions and later imams derived the ‘illah. The three major imams differed: Abu Hanifa (measure + genus), al-Shafi‘i (food + currency), Malik (staple + storability for food; currency for gold/silver).
The hadith of the six commodities is the basis for all ‘illahs.
5
Observe the practical consequences
The difference in ‘illah leads to different rulings on items like iron (prohibited by Hanafis if measured by weight, permitted by Shafi‘is) and eggs (permitted by Hanafis, prohibited by Shafi‘is).
These are known as thamarah al-khilaf (fruits of difference).

Source Text

بيان العام المخصوص
لدخول لام الجنس فيه، وقد خص الله منه الربا، وهو في اللغة: الفضل، ولم يعلم أي فضل ولا عهد الربا يراد به؛ لأن البيع لم يشرع إلا للفضل فهو حينئذٍ نظير الخصوص المجهول، ثم بينه النبي بقوله: "الحنطة بالحنطة والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح، والذهب بالذهب، والفضة بالفضة، مثلاً بمثل يدا بيد والفضل ربا"، فهو حينئذ نظير الخصوص المعلوم، ولكن لم يعلم حال ما سوى الأشياء الستة ألبتة، ولهذا قال عمر رضي الله عنه: "خرج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عنا، ولم يبين لنا أبواب الربا" أي بيانا شافيًا، فاحتاجوا إلى التعليل والاستنباط، فعلّل أبو حنيفة رحله بالقدر والجنس والشافعى رحله بالطعم والثمنية، ومالك رحله بالاقتيات والاذخار، فعمل كل بمقتضى تعليله في تحريم أشياء، وتحليل أشياء على ما يأتي في باب القياس إن شاء الله تعالى.
لا عندنا
وقد خص إلخ أورد أن قوله تعالى: وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا (البقرة: ٢٧٥) ليس كلامًا مستقلاً لاحتياجه إلى ما قبله لرجع الضمير، فكيف يتحقق التخصيص فتأمل. (القمر) الخصوص المعلوم إلخ : فإنه علم أن المراد الفضل على القدر أي الكيل والوزن بدلالة قوله : مثلاً بمثل (القمر) شافيًا : أي بيانا يحتوى على جميع الجزئيات والمواد.(القمر) بالقدر: أي الكيل والوزن، فإذا اجتمع الجنس مع الكيل أو الجنس مع الوزن حرم الربا. (القمر) بالطعم إلخ أي في المطعومات والثمنية أي في الأثمان، فبيع الحديد بالحديد متفاضلا يجوز عند الشافعي رحله وبيع البيضة بالبيضتين يجوز عندنا لا عنده. (القمر) بالاقتيات والاذخار أي في غير الذهب والفضة وأما فيهما فالعلة عند الإمام مالك هو النقدية كما هو عند الشافعي رحله كذا في "معالم التنزيل"، وقال الإمام الرازي في التفسير الكبير": إن العلة عند الإمام مالك هو القوت، أو ما يستصلح به القوت وهو الملح، فما كان من الفاكهة مما يبس فيصير فاكهة يابسة تذخر، وتوكل، فلا يباع بعضه ببعض، إلا يدا بيد، و مثلاً بمثل إذا كان من صنف واحد، فإن كانا من صنفين مختلفين، فلا باس بأن يباع منه اثنان لواحد يدا بيد، ولا يصح إلى أجل وما كان من الفاكهة ولا ييبس ولا يذخر، وإنما يوكل رطبا كالبطيخ والأترج، فجاز أن تؤخذ منه من صنف واحد اثنان بواحد يدا بيد، كذا في المؤطا للإمام مالك رحله
تخريجه . أخر. جه الدرامي، رقم ٦٤/١٢٩ ، باب كراهية الفتيا، وابن ماجه رقم ٢٢٧٦ باب التغليظ في الربا، لفظه عن عمر بن الخطاب قال: إن آخر ما نزلت آية الربا، وإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبض و لم يفسر لنا، فدعوا الربا والريبة.

مبحث العام
۲۰۱
بيان العام المخصوص
عملاً لشبه الاستثناء والنسخ تعليل للمذهب المختار، وبيانه: أن دليل التخصيص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَرَّمَ الرِّباةِ» يشبه الاستثناء باعتبار حكمه، وهو أن المستثنى كما لم يدخل (البقرة: ٢٧٥) فيما قبل، كذلك المخصوص لم يدخل تحت العام ويشبه الناسخ باعتبار صيغته، وهو أن صيغته مستقلة كالناسخ، فيجب علينا أن نراعي كلا الشبهين، ونوفر حظ كل منهما على تقديري كون الخصوص معلومًا ومجهولاً، لا أن نقتصر على الشبه الأول كما اقتصر عليه أي شبه الاستثناء أهل المذهب الثاني، ولا أن نقتصر على الشبه الثاني كما اقتصر عليه أهل المذهب الثالث، أي شبه الناسخ فقلنا: إذا كان دليل الخصوص معلومًا، فرعاية شبه الاستثناء تقتضي أن يبقى العام قطعيًا على حاله لأن المستثنى إذا كان معلوما كان المستثنى منه في الأفراد الباقية على حاله، ورعاية شبه الناسخ تقتضي أن لا يصح الاحتجاج بالعام أصلاً؛ لأن الناسخ مستقل، وكل مستقل يقبل التعليل، وإن لم يقبل الناسخ بنفسه التعليل؛ لئلا تلزم معارضة التعليل النص، وإذا قبل التعليل، يشبه الاستثناء ولذا اشترط اقترانه بالعام كما اشترط اقتران الاستثناء بالمستثنى منه . (القمر) معلومًا ومجهولاً : أي معلوم المراد عند السامع ومجهوله. (القمر) المذهب الثاني: وهو أنه يسقط الاحتجاج بالعام عند لحوق الخصوص كما سيجيء. (القمر) المذهب الثالث: وهو أنه يبقى العالم قطعيًا بعد لحوق الخصوص كما كان.(القمر) لأن الناسخ :إلخ :توضيحه أن الناسخ مستقل تام وكل مستقل تام يقبل التعليل، فإن الأصل في الأحكام الشرعية أن يكون معللاً، فالناسخ يقبل التعليل أيضًا، وإذا قبل المخصص التعليل إلخ، ثم اعلم أن قبول الناسخ التعليل باعتبار استقلال الصيغة وأما باعتبار حكمه فلا يقبل التعليل، والمخصص شبيه بالناسخ، فهو يقبل التعليل، لأن حكمه رفع الحكم باعتبار المعارضة والمدافعة بعد الثبوت، والتعليل لا يعارض النص؛ لأنه دون النص، فلا ينسخ النص، فالناسخ لا يقبل التعليل بنفسه أي باعتبار حكمه، وإلا يلزم معارضة التعليل النص المنسوخ، وهو باطل، ولا يلزم هذه المعارضة في المخصص إذا يقبل التعليل، فإن حكمه ليس رفع الحكم بعد ثبوته بطريق المعارضة على ما سيجيء. وإن لم يقبل إلخ رد لوهم تقرير الوهم: أنه كيف جوزتم التعليل في المخصوص اعتبارًا بشبه الناسخ مع أنه لا يجري فيه التعليل، وتقرير الدفع أن الناسخ المعلوم إذا ورد في بعض ما تناوله العام يصح تعليله، لكنه لم يعلل
Chapter on General (al-'Amm) / Explanation of the Specified General: Because the lam of genus enters it, and Allah specified riba from it, and riba linguistically means excess. It was not known which excess or what pledge of riba was intended; because sale was only legislated for profit, so it was like an unspecified specification. Then the Prophet explained it with his saying: "Wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, gold for gold, silver for silver, equal amounts, hand to hand, and excess is riba." So then it was like a known specification, but the case of items other than these six was not known at all. Therefore 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: "The Prophet (peace be upon him) passed away from us without explaining the types of riba to us" meaning a sufficient explanation. So they needed ta'lil (rational explanation) and istinbat (derivation). So Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) explained it with measure (qadr) and genus (jins); al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) with food (tu'm) and being currency (thumaniyya); and Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) with being a staple food (iqtitat) and being storable (iddikhar). Each acted according to his ta'lil in prohibiting and permitting things, as will come in the chapter on qiyas, Allah willing. / Not according to us. / 'And He specified etc.' It is objected that the verse "and He prohibited riba" (2:275) is not an independent statement because it needs what comes before it due to the pronoun reference, so how does specification occur? Ponder. (al-Qamar) 'known specification etc.': It is known that what is meant is excess over the measure (i.e., volume and weight) by the indication of his saying 'equal amounts'. (al-Qamar) 'sufficient': meaning an explanation containing all the particulars and matters. (al-Qamar) 'by measure': i.e., volume and weight; when genus combines with volume or genus with weight, riba is prohibited. (al-Qamar) 'by food etc.' i.e., in foodstuffs, and 'thumaniyya' i.e., in currencies. So selling iron for iron with a difference is permissible according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and selling one egg for two eggs is permissible according to us, not according to him. (al-Qamar) 'by being a staple and storable' i.e., in other than gold and silver; as for gold and silver, the cause according to Imam Malik is currency as it is according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). This is in 'Ma'alim al-Tanzil'. And Imam al-Razi said in al-Tafsir al-Kabir: The cause according to Imam Malik is staple food or what is used to improve staple food, i.e., salt. So among fruits, what dries and becomes dry fruit stored and eaten, cannot be sold one for another unless hand to hand and equal amounts if of the same type; if they are of different types, then it is permissible to sell two for one hand to hand, and it is not valid for credit. And among fruits, what does not dry nor is stored, but is eaten fresh like watermelon and citron, it is permissible to take two of one type for one hand to hand. This is in al-Muwatta' of Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him). / Its extraction: Recorded by al-Darimi, no. 64/129, chapter on dislike of giving fatwa; and Ibn Majah, no. 2276, chapter on severity regarding riba, wording from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: "Indeed the last thing revealed was the verse of riba, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) passed away without explaining it to us, so leave riba and doubt." / / Chapter on al-'Amm, page 201 / Explanation of the Specified General / Acting upon the resemblance to exception (istithna') and abrogation (naskh) is the justification for the chosen madhhab. Its explanation: That the evidence of specification, i.e., the verse "and He prohibited riba" (2:275), resembles exception in terms of its ruling, i.e., just as the excepted item does not enter into what precedes, similarly the specified item does not enter under the general. And it resembles abrogation in terms of its formulation, i.e., its formulation is independent like that of an abrogating text. So we must consider both resemblances and give each its due share on the two possibilities of the specification being known or unknown, not restricting ourselves to the first resemblance (that of exception) as the people of the second madhhab did, nor restricting ourselves to the second resemblance (that of abrogation) as the people of the third madhhab did. So we say: When the evidence of specification is known, then observing the resemblance of exception requires that the general remain definitive (qat'i) as it was, because when the excepted item is known, the thing from which it is excepted remains as it is with respect to the remaining individuals. And observing the resemblance of abrogation requires that argumentation with the general is not valid at all, because the abrogator is independent, and every independent thing is subject to ta'lil, even if the abrogator itself does not accept ta'lil (to avoid conflict of ta'lil with the text). And if it accepts ta'lil, it resembles exception; therefore it was required that it (the specification) be attached to the general, just as exception is required to be attached to the thing from which it is excepted. (al-Qamar) 'known and unknown': i.e., the intended meaning known to the listener or unknown. (al-Qamar) 'the second madhhab': which holds that argumentation with the general is dropped when specification occurs, as will come. (al-Qamar) 'the third madhhab': which holds that the general remains definitive after specification as it was. (al-Qamar) 'because the abrogator etc.': Explanation: The abrogator is fully independent, and every fully independent thing accepts ta'lil; indeed the original principle in legal rulings is that they are subject to ta'lil. So the abrogator also accepts ta'lil. And if the specification accepts ta'lil etc. Then know that the abrogator's acceptance of ta'lil is with respect to the independence of the formulation; as for its ruling, it does not accept ta'lil. And the specification is similar to the abrogator, so it accepts ta'lil, because its ruling is the removal of a ruling by way of opposition and defense after establishment, and ta'lil does not oppose the text because it is inferior to the text, so it does not abrogate the text. Thus the abrogator does not accept ta'lil by itself, i.e., with respect to its ruling; otherwise, opposition of ta'lil to the abrogated text would be necessary, which is invalid. And this opposition does not occur in the specification if it accepts ta'lil, because its ruling is not the removal of a ruling after its establishment by way of opposition, as will come. 'And if it does not accept etc.' is a response to a misconception: The misconception: How did you permit ta'lil in the specified text considering its resemblance to abrogation, while it (the abrogator) does not accept ta'lil? The response: That the known abrogator, when it occurs in part of what the general includes, its ta'lil is valid, but it was not subject to ta'lil.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar discusses the nature of a general text (al-'amm) after it has been specified (takhsis). The chapter is on 'al-'amm al-makhsoos' (the specified general). The author uses the Quranic prohibition of riba (2:275) as a key example. The verse 'and Allah prohibited riba' is general because the word 'riba' includes all types of usury. However, the Prophet ﷺ specified it by mentioning six commodities and the condition of equality and hand-to-hand exchange, thereby defining riba as excess in specific items. The passage explains that before this specification, the term was like an unknown specification (khusus majhul), but after the hadith, it became a known specification (khusus ma'lum). Nonetheless, the ruling on other items not mentioned remained unclear, leading the Companions like 'Umar to seek further explanation. This led the fuqaha' to perform ijtihad to deduce the effective cause ('illah) for riba. The passage then presents the positions of the three major imams: Imam Abu Hanifa held that the 'illah is measure (kil or wazn) combined with genus; Imam al-Shafi'i held that it is food (tu'm) and currency (thumaniyya); Imam Malik held that it is staple food (iqtitat) and storability (iddikhar) for non-monetary items, and currency for gold and silver. The commentary then lists some fiqh implications: according to Shafi'i, selling iron for iron with disparity is permissible (since iron is not a food nor a currency); according to Hanafis, selling one egg for two is permissible (since eggs are measured by count, not by weight or volume? Actually Hanafis consider eggs as measured by count, but the text says 'when' so we need to be careful). The passage then moves to the usul discussion: How should we treat a general that has been specified? Some scholars (madhhab thani) say argumentation with the general becomes invalid (like exception), some (madhhab thalith) say the general remains qat'i (like it was never affected). The Hanafi chosen position (al-mukhtar) is a middle ground: When the specification is known, the general remains qat'i in its remaining application, but it also becomes open to ta'lil (rational explanation for qiyas) due to its resemblance to naskh (abrogation) in terms of independent formulation. This allows analogical extension to other items not mentioned, as the 'illah can be derived. The passage details this reasoning, explaining why the specified general resembles both exception (in ruling) and abrogation (in formulation). This is a sophisticated usul principle that balances textual certainty with the need for ijtihad.

Key Terms
العام المخصوص (al-'amm al-makhsoos): A general term that has been partially specified by a separate evidence, removing some of its potential referents.
التخصيص (takhsis): The act of limiting the scope of a general term by specifying an evidence that excludes some individuals or types.
العلة (al-'illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that determines the application of a legal ruling, derived through ijtihad.
شبه الاستثناء (shabah al-istithna'): Resemblance to exception: like excepted items, the specified items never fell under the general.
شبه الناسخ (shabah al-naskh): Resemblance to abrogation: the specifying evidence has an independent formulation like an abrogator.
قطعي (qat'i): Definitive; a ruling or text that is certain in its meaning or transmission.
تعليل (ta'lil): Rational explanation; the process of finding an effective cause ('illah) for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi chosen position, what is the status of a general text after it has been specified by a known evidence?
A) It becomes completely invalid.
B) It remains qat'i for the remaining individuals and is open to ta'lil.
C) It remains qat'i but cannot be subject to qiyas.
D) It becomes zanni and requires further evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: a specified general remains hujja for the unexcluded instances and allows derivation of an 'illah for analogical extension.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
The Effect of an Unknown Specificator on the General Term
Explaining the epistemological status of a general term after unknown specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a general term that has been specified by an unknown specificator, and apply it to a contractual scenario involving an option.

Core Idea
A general term specified by an unknown specificator loses its certainty but remains a valid legal proof — a middle ground between exception and abrogation.

In Hanafi usul, the general term (ʿāmm) is considered definitive (qaṭʿī) in its indication until a specificator (mukhaṣṣiṣ) is proven. But what happens when the specificator exists but its exact extent is unknown? This passage explores the epistemological status of such a term. The Hanafi approach balances two conflicting analogies: the specificator resembles an exception (istithnāʾ), which would nullify the general's usability, and an abrogation (naskh), which would leave it definitive. The resolution is a middle ground: the general loses its certainty but remains a valid proof. The author illustrates this with a detailed fiqh analogy involving a sale of two slaves with an option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul problem
Recognize that a general term (ʿāmm) has been specified by a specificator (mukhaṣṣiṣ) whose extent is unknown. This creates uncertainty about the remaining scope.
2
Recognize the two competing resemblances
Consider that the specificator resembles an exception (istithnāʾ) because it removes some individuals, and also resembles an abrogation (naskh) because it contradicts the initial apparent generality.
Exception would make the general completely unknown; abrogation would leave it definitive because the abrogator is unknown and thus drops.
3
Understand the Hanafi compromise
The Hanafi position balances the two resemblances: the general loses its definitive status (qaṭʿī) but remains a valid proof (ḥujja). It is between the two extremes.
Phrase from the text: 'لا يبقى قطعيًا، ولكن يصح التمسك به'
4
Analyze the fiqh analogy
Examine the sale of two slaves with an option for the seller to return one. This case has four scenarios depending on whether the subject and price of the option are known or not.
The slave with the option is included in the contract but not in the ruling, resembling both abrogation and exception.
5
Derive the ruling from the analogy
When both the locus of the option and its price are known, the sale is valid due to the predominance of the resemblance to abrogation. This parallels the usul rule: if the specificator's extent were known, the general would be definitive in the remaining; if unknown, it is not definitive but still usable.
The first scenario in the analogy corresponds to a known specificator; the others to unknown or partially known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يدري كم يخرج بالتعليل، وكم بقي فيصير مجهولاً، وجهالته تؤثر في جهالة العام، فلا يصح التمسك به. ورعاية شبه الناسخ تقتضي أن يبقى العام قطعيًا؛ لأن الناسخ المجهول يسقط بنفسه، فلرعاية الشبهين جعلنا العام بين بين وقلنا: لا يبقى قطعيًا، ولكن يصح التمسك به. نظير هذه المسألة الفقهية وهي أن يعين الخيار في أحد العبدين المبيعين، وسمي ثمنه؛ وذلك لأن هذه المسألة على أربعة أوجه: أحدها أن يعين محل الخيار ويسمى ثمنه، والثاني: أن لا يعين ولا يسمى، والثالث: أن يعين ولا يسمى، والرابع: أن يسمى ولا يعين، فالأول صحيح لشبه الناسخ، والثاني فاسد لجهالة الثمن والمبيع، والثالث فاسد لجهالة الثمن، والرابع فاسد لجهالة المبيع. فالعبد الذي فيه الخيار داخل في العقد غير داخل في الحكم، فمن حيث إنه داخل في العقد يكون رد المبيع بخيار الشرط تبديلاً، فيكون كالنسخ، ومن حيث إنه غير داخل في الحكم يكون رده بيان أنه لم يدخل فيكون كالاستثناء، فيكون كالمخصص الذي له شبه بالاستثناء، وشبه بالنسخ، فرعاية شبه النسخ تقتضي صحة البيع في الصور الأربع؛ لأن كلا من العبدين بالنظر إلى الإيجاب مبيع ببيع واحد، فلا يكون بيعًا بالحصة ابتداء، بل بقاء. ورعاية شبه الاستثناء تقتضي فساد البيع في الصور الأربع لجعل ما ليس بمبيع شرطًا لقبول المبيع، فلرعاية الشبهين قلنا: إن علم محل الخيار وثمنه، وهو المذكور في المتن صح البيع لشبه الناسخ.
So it is not known how much is excluded by the [unknown] cause [of specification], and how much remains, thus it becomes unknown, and its ignorance affects the ignorance of the general term, so it is not valid to adhere to it. And consideration of the resemblance to abrogation requires that the general remains definitive, because the unknown abrogator falls by itself. So due to consideration of both resemblances, we have made the general between the two and we said: it does not remain definitive, but it is valid to adhere to it. The analogy for this is the juristic case where the option [of repudiation] is specified in one of the two sold slaves, and its price is named; because this case has four aspects: first, that the locus of the option is specified and its price is named; second, that it is neither specified nor named; third, that it is specified but not named; fourth, that it is named but not specified. The first is valid due to resemblance to abrogation, the second is invalid due to ignorance of the price and the sold item, the third is invalid due to ignorance of the price, the fourth is invalid due to ignorance of the sold item. The slave in which the option resides is included in the contract but not included in the ruling. So insofar as it is included in the contract, the return of the sold item due to the option of condition is an exchange, thus it is like abrogation; and insofar as it is not included in the ruling, its return is an indication that it was not included, thus it is like an exception. So it is like a specificator that has resemblance to exception and resemblance to abrogation. So consideration of resemblance to abrogation requires the validity of the sale in all four forms, because each of the two slaves, with respect to the offer, is sold in a single sale, so it is not a sale by share initially but by continuance. Consideration of resemblance to exception requires the invalidity of the sale in all four forms, because it makes what is not sold a condition for accepting the sold item. So due to consideration of both resemblances, we say: if the locus of the option and its price are known—as mentioned in the text—the sale is valid due to resemblance to abrogation.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This lesson is an expansion on the rule regarding the general term (al-'āmm) after it has been specified by a specificator (al-mukhaṣṣiṣ) whose precise extent is unknown. The author, following the Hanafi method, examines two competing analogies: the specificator resembles an exception (istithnā') in that it removes some individuals from the general, but it also resembles an abrogator (nāsikh) because it contradicts the initial apparent meaning. If the specificator were like an exception, ignorance of its extent would make the general completely unknown and unusable; if like an abrogation, the abrogator being unknown would simply drop, leaving the general definitive. The Hanafi position strikes a middle ground: the general loses its definitive status (qaṭ'ī) but remains a valid proof (ḥujja) because doubt does not overturn certainty that originally existed. The author illustrates this with a fiqh example: selling two slaves in one transaction with an option for the seller to return one. The option creates a situation analogous to specification. The case has four scenarios depending on whether the slave subject to the option and its price are specified or not. The conclusion is that if both are known, the sale is valid, because the resemblance to abrogation (which would allow the contract to stand) outweighs the resemblance to exception (which would invalidate it). This shows how Hanafi usul applies analogical reasoning and balances conflicting indications to derive rulings.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category without limit.
خاص (khāṣṣ): A specificator that restricts the scope of a general term.
دليل الخصوص (dalīl al-khuṣūṣ): The evidence that indicates the specification of a general term.
مجهول (majhūl): Unknown in extent or identity, leading to uncertainty.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; removal of a ruling by a later evidence.
استثناء (istithnāʾ): Exception; removal of some individuals from a general term by an explicit proviso.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is the effect of an unknown specificator (mukhaṣṣiṣ majhūl) on a general term (ʿāmm)?
A) The general term becomes completely invalid and cannot be used as evidence.
B) The general term loses its definitive status (qaṭʿī) but remains valid as a proof (ḥujja).
C) The general term remains definitive (qaṭʿī) exactly as before.
D) The general term becomes speculative but its usage is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
A general term that has been specified by an unknown specificator loses its definitive status but remains a valid legal proof, a middle ground between exception and abrogation.

Applying Usul Principles: Khiyar al-Shart in Multi-Item Sales
Analysis of khiyar shart via qiyas to naskh and istithna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of qiyas, naskh, and istithna to determine the validity of a khiyar shart in a multi-item sale, and distinguish the four scenarios based on knowledge of the subject and price.

Core Idea
A sale with an option on one item resembles both abrogation and exception; validity hinges on known subject and price.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the validity of a conditional option (khiyar al-shart) in a sale involving multiple items is determined by balancing two analogical resemblances: abrogation (naskh) and exception (istithna). This lesson unpacks the four possible scenarios from this passage, showing how the knowledge of the option's subject and price tips the scale. By tracing the reasoning, you will learn to apply these principles to similar contractual stipulations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Scenarios
The passage outlines four cases regarding whether the subject of the option (the slave) and its price are specified. Note which are known and which are unknown in each example.
Examples: (1) subject and price known, (2) both unknown, (3) subject known but price unknown, (4) price known but subject unknown.
2
Recognize the Two Analogies
Understand that the option's effect is likened to naskh (abrogation) when it cancels part of the contract like a later ruling abrogates an earlier one, and to istithna (exception) when it excludes the subject from the contract initially.
Naskh suggests validity, istithna suggests invalidity.
3
Analyze the Conflict of Analogies
Each analogy leads to a different outcome in all four cases. The Hanafi solution weighs both and gives priority to naskh when the subject and price are known, making the sale valid; otherwise, istithna prevails, making it invalid.
The decisive factor is knowledge (jahl vs. 'ilm).
4
Apply to the Examples
Work through the four examples provided: sold Zayd and Amr together with option on Zayd knowing price, etc. Verify which scenarios are valid or invalid per the rule.
Example 1: valid; Example 2-4: invalid due to ignorance of price subject, or both.
5
Contrast with the Free-Slave Case
The passage notes that combining a free person (non-saleable) with a slave is invalid even if prices are separate, because the free person is not a valid subject. This reinforces that the inclusion of a saleable item (the slave under option) does not violate contract requisites.
This contrast clarifies the scope of the rule.

Source Text

مبحث العام
بيان العام المخصوص
هو جائز ثمنه، وذلك لأن هذه المسألة على أربعة أوجه أحدها أن يُعين محل الخيار ويسمى والثاني: أن لا يعين ولا يسمى، والثالث: أن يعين ولا يسمى والرابع: أن يسمى ولا يعين، فاسد الجهالة الثمن والمبيع فاسد لجهالة الثمن هو أيضا فاسد لجهالة المبيع فالعبد الذي فيه الخيار داخل في العقد غير داخل في الحكم فمن حيث إنه داخل في العقد يكون رد المبيع بخيار الشرط تبديلاً، فيكون كالنسخ، ومن حيث إنه غير داخل في الحكم يكون رده بيان أنه لم يدخل فيكون كالاستثناء، فيكون كالمخصص الذي له شبه بالاستثناء، وشبه بالنسخ، فرعاية شبه النسخ تقتضي صحة البيع في الصور الأربع؛ لأن كلا من العبدين بالنظر إلى الإيجاب مبيع ببيع واحد، فلا يكون بيعًا بالحصة ابتداء، بل بقاء. ورعاية شبه الاستثناء تقتضي فساد البيع في الصور الأربع لجعل ما ليس بمبيع شرطًا لقبول المبيع، فلرعاية الشبهين قلنا: إن علم محل الخيار وثمنه، وهو المذكور في المتن صح البيع لشبه الناسخ، على أربعة أوجه مثال الأول: كما إذا باع زيدًا وعمروا بيعًا واحدا كلا منهما بخمس مائة على أن البائع بالخيار في زيد ثلاثة أيام ومثال الثاني باعهما بألف على أنه بالخيار في أحدهما من غير تعيين لثمن كل، ولا لما فيه الخيار. ومثال الثالث: باعهما بألف من غير تفصيل الثمن على أنه بالخيار في زيد. ومثال الرابع: باعهما بألف كلا منهما بخمس مائة على أنه بالخيار في أحدهما. ثم: لم يعتبر ههنا جعل قبول ما ليس بمبيع شرطًا لقبول المبيع، كما اعتبر إذا جمع بين الحر والعبد وفصل الثمن؛ لأن الحر لم يكن محلاً للبيع واشتراط قبوله ليس من مقتضيات العقد، وفي مسألتنا العبد الذي فيه الخيار داخل في العقد، فلا يكون ضمه مخالفًا لمقتضى العقد، وإن جهل أحدهما أو كلاهما لا يصح لشبه الاستثناء، ففي صورة جهل كليهما يصير البيع كأنه قال: بعت هذين العبدين بألف إلا أحدهما بحصة ذلك، وذلك باطل، وفي صورة جهل المبيع يصير كأنه قال: بعت هذين العبدين بألف إلا أحدهما بخمس مائة، وفي صورة جهل الثمن يصير كأنه قال: بعتهما بألف إلا هذا بحصة من الألف، ولم يعتبر في هذه الصور شبه الناسخ؛ لأن الناسخ المجهول يسقط بنفسه، فيبطل شرط الخيار، ويلزم العقد في العبدين، وهو خلاف ما قصده القائل.
Section on the General. Explanation of the General that is Specific. It is valid with its price. That is because this issue has four aspects: first, that the subject of the option is specified and named; second, that it is not specified and not named; third, that it is specified but not named; fourth, that it is named but not specified. Invalid due to ignorance of price and object. Invalid due to ignorance of price. Also invalid due to ignorance of object. The slave who has the option is included in the contract but not included in the ruling. Insofar as it is included in the contract, returning the sold item by option of stipulation is a substitution, thus like abrogation. Insofar as it is not included in the ruling, its return is a declaration that it was not included, thus like exception, and thus like the specific that has resemblance to exception and resemblance to abrogation. Considering the resemblance to abrogation requires validity of the sale in the four cases because each of the two slaves, with respect to the offer, is sold in one sale, so it is not a sale by share initially but perpetually. Considering the resemblance to exception requires invalidity of the sale in the four cases because it makes what is not sold a condition for accepting the sold item. So considering the two resemblances, we said: if the subject of the option and its price are known, which is mentioned in the text, the sale is valid due to the resemblance to the abrogator. In four aspects: example of the first: as if he sold Zayd and Amr in one sale, each for five hundred, on condition that the seller has an option regarding Zayd for three days. Example of the second: he sold both for one thousand on condition that he has an option regarding one of them without specifying the price of each nor the subject of the option. Example of the third: he sold both for one thousand without detailing the price on condition that he has an option regarding Zayd. Example of the fourth: he sold both for one thousand, each for five hundred, on condition that he has an option regarding one of them. Then: here, making acceptance of what is not sold a condition for accepting the sold item is not considered, as it is considered when he combines a free person and a slave and separates the price, because the free person was not a subject of sale and stipulating its acceptance is not among the requisites of the contract. In our issue, the slave who has the option is included in the contract, so his inclusion does not contradict the requisite of the contract. If either or both are unknown, the sale is not valid due to the resemblance to exception. So in the case of ignorance of both, the sale becomes as if he said: I sold these two slaves for one thousand except one of them for a share of that, and that is invalid. In the case of ignorance of the object, it becomes as if he said: I sold these two slaves for one thousand except one of them for five hundred. In the case of ignorance of the price, it becomes as if he said: I sold them for one thousand except this one for a share of the thousand. And in these cases, the resemblance to the abrogator is not considered because the unknown abrogator drops by itself, so the condition of option becomes void and the contract becomes binding for both slaves, which is contrary to what the speaker intended.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work explains the ruling on a sale with a stipulation of option (khiyar shart) when multiple items are sold together, using analogies to naskh (abrogation) and istithna (exception). The author presents four scenarios regarding whether the subject of the option (the slave with the option) and its price are specified or not. The ruling is that if both are known, the sale is valid; otherwise, it is invalid. The reasoning balances two analogies: the option resembles abrogation in that it modifies the contract, suggesting validity; but it also resembles exception in that it excludes part of the transaction, suggesting invalidity. Ultimately, the Hanafi position is that knowledge of both the subject and price tips the balance toward validity due to the resemblance to abrogation, while ignorance leads to invalidity due to the resemblance to exception. The text also compares this to the case of selling a free person and slave together, where the free person is not a valid subject of sale, so the contract is invalid even if price is separated.

Key Terms
العام المخصوص (al-'amm al-makhsus): The general term that is specified by a particular exception or condition, here applied to the sale with khiyar.
الناسخ (al-nasikh): The abrogator; here analogically the exercise of the option cancels part of the contract like naskh.
الاستثناء (al-istithna): Exception; the option is likened to an exception that excludes the subject from the sale initially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analysis of khiyar shart with two slaves, in which scenario does the resemblance to naskh (abrogation) outweigh the resemblance to istithna (exception)?
A) When the subject of the option and its price are both specified.
B) When the subject is unspecified but the price is known.
C) When the price is unspecified but the subject is known.
D) When both subject and price are unspecified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances analogies to naskh and istithna; a sale with an option on a specific item is valid only when both the option's subject and its price are known, otherwise ignorance causes invalidity.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Dispute Over the Specified General Text (al-amm al-makhsus)
Hanafi usul dispute on probative value of specified general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on the probative value of a specified general text and apply the analogy to an unknown exception.

Core Idea
Specification can nullify a general text entirely—some Hanafis liken it to an unknown exception.

In this passage from Noor al-Anwar, we encounter a crucial dispute within the Hanafi school: does a general text (amm) retain any probative value after it has been specified (makhsus)? While some scholars maintain that the general remains partially valid if the specifier is known, others—led by al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban—argue that specification destroys the general's authority entirely, regardless of whether the specifier is known or unknown. This lesson dissects their arguments and the key analogy to an unknown exception (istithna majhul).

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Determine the precise question: What is the probative value (hujjiyya) of a general text that has been specified by a separate evidence?
The dispute is about whether the general remains a proof for the remaining individuals.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Clearly articulate both positions: (1) The general remains a proof unless the specifier is unknown; (2) The general loses all probative value, analogous to an unknown exception, irrespective of whether the specifier is known or unknown.
The second position is attributed to al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban.
3
Examine the analogy to unknown exception
Understand the qiyas: Both specification and exception indicate non-inclusion. If the scope of exclusion is unknown, the remainder becomes unknown, so the general cannot be used as evidence.
The key operative phrase: 'لأن كل واحد منهما لبيان أنه لم يدخل' (each indicates non-entry).
4
Distinguish between known and unknown specifier
The first view argues that a known specifier leaves a known remainder. The second view counters that even if the specifier is known, the exact amount excluded is unknown, leading to ignorance of the remainder.
The second view extends the analogy to both cases, claiming rational analysis ('bā al-ta'līl') renders the known specifier effectively unknown.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Apply the dispute to an example: 'Kill the polytheists' specified by 'Do not kill dhimmis'. The first view allows using the general for non-dhimmi polytheists; the second view blocks any deduction from the general.
The author of Noor al-Anwar appears to favor the first view, referring to the second as extreme ('faratu').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث العام
بيان العام المخصوص
ولم يعتبر ههنا جعل قبول ما ليس بمبيع شرطًا لقبول المبيع، كما اعتبر إذا جمع بين الحر والعبد وفصل الثمن؛ لأن الحر لم يكن محلاً للبيع واشتراط قبوله ليس من مقتضيات العقد، وفي مسألتنا العبد الذي فيه الخيار داخل في العقد، فلا يكون ضمه مخالفًا لمقتضى العقد، وإن جهل أحدهما أو كلاهما لا يصح لشبه الاستثناء، ففي صورة جهل كليهما يصير البيع كأنه قال: بعت هذين العبدين بألف إلا احدهما بحصة ذلك، وذلك باطل، وفي صورة جهل المبيع يصير كأنه قال: بعت هذين العبدين بألف إلا أحدهما بخمس مائة، وفي صورة جهل الثمن يصير كأنه قال: بعتهما بألف إلا هذا بحصة من الألف، ولم يعتبر في هذه الصور شبه الناسخ ؛ لأن الناسخ المجهول يسقط بنفسه، فيبطل شرط الخيار، ويلزم العقد في العبدين، وهو خلاف ما قصده القائل.
الثلاث
ولم يعتبر إلخ أي لم يعتبر ههنا شبه الاستثناء حتى يفسد هذا البيع بالشرط الفاسد، وهو جعل قبول إلخ.(القمر) ولم يعتبر ههنا إلخ هذا جواب شبهة، وهي أن يقول: ينبغي أن يفسد العقد في هذه الصورة أيضا، لوجود وهو قبول العقد في الذي لم يدخل في العقد، لأن العبد الذي فيه الخيار غير داخل حكمًا كما إذا جمع بين حرّ وقن، فإنه لا يجوز العقد في القن، وإن فصل الثمن؛ لما أنه جعل قبول العقد في الحر شرطًا لصحة العقد في القن والجواب: أن قبول العقد في الذي فيه الخيار وإن كان شرطًا لانعقاده في الآخر، ولكن هذا غير مفسد للعقد؛ لكونه محلاً للبيع، وهناك الحر لم يكن محلاً للبيع، فصار هذا كما إذا جمع بين قن ومدبر. (السنبلي) إذا جمع إلخ : أي باع الحر والعبد بالألف صفقة واحدة وبين ثمن كل منهما، فهذا البيع فاسد في العبد عند أبي حنيفة له على ما سيجيء. (القمر) لأن إلخ علة لقوله ولم يعتبر إلخ. (القمر) لم يكن إلخ فإن محل البيع هو المال المتقوم، والحر ليس كذلك على ما مرّ، فليس الحر داخلاً، لا في العقد، ولا في الحكم، فاشتراط قبوله مفسد للبيع. (القمر) داخل إلخ: فاشتراط قبوله اشتراط مبيع بالنظر إلى العقد، فليس هو كالحر. (القمر) وذلك باطل: لجهالة المبيع، فإنه إذا اشترط الخيار في أحد العبدين بلا عين لزم العقد في العبد الآخر، وهو مجهول ولجهالة الثمن؛ لأنه لو ثبت الحكم في العبد الذي لا خيار فيه لثبت بحصة من الثمن ابتداء مجهولة. (القمر) وهو خلاف ما قصده القائل: أي العاقد البائع لأن إقدامه على بيع العبدين مع أحدهما، وعدم الاكتفاء على البيع الصرف دليل على أن لزوم البيع فيهما غير مقصود له. (القمر)
وهي الخيار في
هذا العام المخصوص
وقيل إنه يسقط الاحتجاج به كالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأن كل واحد منهما لبيان أنه لم يدخل، هو المذهب الثاني، وإليه ذهب الكرخي وعيسى بن أبان، وهؤلاء قد فرطوا في هذا العام المخصوص البعض، ويقولون : لا يبقى العام قابلاً للتمسك أصلاً، سواء كان المخصوص معلومًا كما إذا قيل: اقتلوا المشركين ولا تقتلوا أهل الذمة"، أو مجهولاً كما إذا قيل: "اقتلوا المشركين ولا تقتلوا بعضهم، وشبهوه بالاستثناء فقط؛ لأنهم لم يراعوا جانب الصيغة بل اعتبروا المعنى فقط وهو عدم الدخول، وإنما شبهوه بالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأنه إذا كان دليل المخصوص مجهولا، فظاهر أنه كالمجهول وإن كان معلومًا، فبالتعليل لا بالناسخ أي كالاستثناء يصير مجهولاً، وإن كان الاستثناء في نفسه مما لا يقبل التعليل.
فصار كالبيع المضاف إلى حرّ و عبد بثمن ،واحد تشبيه لدليل هذا المذهب بمسألة فقهية مذكورة، فإنه إذا باع العبد والحر بثمن واحد بأن يقول: "بعتهما بالألف،" فالحر لا يدخل في البيع، فيكون استثناء،
يسقط إلخ أي لا يبقى العام حجة لا قطعية ولا ظنية كالاستثناء إلخ يعني أن المخصص كالاستثناء المجهول، وجهالة الاستثناء توجب جهالة المستثنى منه، فيكون الباقي مجهولاً ، فكذا جهالة المخصص توجب جهالة العام، فلا يبقى العام حجة. لأن كل واحد إلخ: دليل للإلحاق المستفاد من كاف التشبيه في قوله كالاستثناء المجهول أي إنما ألحق المخصص بالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأن كل واحد منهما أي من المخصص والاستثناء المجهول لبيان إلخ، فالاستثناء يبين أن المستثنى لم يدخل في صدر الكلام، فكذا المخصص يدل على أن المخصوص لم يدخل تحت العام. (القمر) وإنما شبهوه إلخ : دفع دخل تقريره أن تشبيه العام المخصوص منه بالاستثناء المجهول صحيح إذا كان الخصوص أي المخصص مجهولاً ، وأما إذا كان معلوماً ، فلا، وتقرير الدفع ظاهر. (السنبلي فبالتعليل إلخ يعني أن المخصص المعلوم لاستقلاله يقبل التعليل، ولم يعرف أن أي قدر خرج، فصار المخرج مجهولاً، فبقي الباقي مجهولاً. (القمر) مما لا يقبل التعليل: لأن الاستثناء ليس بنص مستقل، بل بمنزلة وصف قائم بفحوى الكلام دال على عدم دخول المستثنى منه والعدم لا يعلل. (المحشي)
Subject: The General. Explanation of the specified general. And he did not consider here making the acceptance of what is not a sold item a condition for accepting the sold item, as was considered when combining a free person and a slave and specifying the price; because the free person was not a valid subject for sale and stipulating his acceptance is not a requirement of the contract, and in our case the slave who has the option is included in the contract, so his inclusion does not oppose the requirements of the contract. If one of them or both are unknown, it is not valid due to resemblance to exception. In the case of both being unknown, the sale becomes as if he said: 'I sold these two slaves for a thousand except one of them for its share,' and that is invalid. In the case of the sold item being unknown, it becomes as if he said: 'I sold these two slaves for a thousand except one of them for five hundred.' In the case of the price being unknown, it becomes as if he said: 'I sold them for a thousand except this one for a share of the thousand.' And he did not consider in these forms the resemblance to abrogation because an unknown abrogator abrogates by itself, so the option condition becomes void, and the contract is binding on both slaves, which is contrary to the speaker's intent. ... This is the specified general. And it is said that it loses its validity as a proof like an unknown exception; because each of them is to indicate that it did not enter. This is the second madhhab, and al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban adhered to it. They went to extremes regarding this specified general part, and they say: the general does not remain capable of being used as evidence at all, whether the specified part is known, as if one says: 'Kill the polytheists and do not kill the people of the dhimmah,' or unknown, as if one says: 'Kill the polytheists and do not kill some of them.' And they analogized it to exception only because they did not consider the aspect of wording but only considered the meaning, which is non-inclusion. They analogized it to the unknown exception because if the evidence of the specified is unknown, then apparently it is like an unknown, and if it is known, then by rational analysis, not by abrogation, like exception it becomes unknown, even though exception in itself is not subject to rational analysis. So it becomes like a sale attributed to a free person and a slave for one price, analogizing the evidence of this madhhab to a mentioned fiqhi issue: when one sells a slave and a free person for one price, saying 'I sold them for a thousand,' the free person is not included in the sale, so it becomes an exception. ... 'It loses its validity' meaning: the general remains a proof neither definitive nor presumptive, like exception, meaning that the specifier is like an unknown exception, and the ignorance of the exception causes ignorance of the excepted-from, so the remaining becomes unknown; similarly, ignorance of the specifier causes ignorance of the general, so the general does not remain a proof. ... (al-Qamar) ... (al-Sunbuliy) ... (al-Muhashi)
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar discusses the legal status of a general text (amm) after it has been specified (makhsus). It presents a dispute among Hanafi usul scholars: some hold that specification does not eliminate the probative value of the general text entirely, while others, notably al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban, argue that specification renders the general text completely invalid as a proof, likening it to an unknown exception (istithna majhul). The commentary uses a fiqhi example of selling a slave with an option condition to illustrate the difference between known and unknown specification. It explains that if the specifier is unknown, the remaining general becomes unknown and thus cannot be used as evidence. If the specifier is known, they argue that the exact amount excluded becomes unknown, leading to ignorance of the remaining general. The passage also distinguishes between specification and abrogation (naskh), noting that an unknown abrogator annuls itself, whereas an unknown specifier causes uncertainty. The commentary by al-Qamar, al-Sunbuliy, and al-Muhashi clarifies the analogies and rebuts potential objections.

Key Terms
العام المخصوص (al-amm al-makhsus): A general term that has been specified by a separate legal evidence, removing some of its individuals.
الاستثناء المجهول (al-istithna al-majhul): An exception whose excepted part is unknown, causing the excepted-from to be unknown.
المخصص (al-mukhassis): The evidence that specifies a general term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second madhhab (al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban), what is the status of a specified general text?
A) It remains a definitive proof.
B) It remains a presumptive proof.
C) It loses all probative value like an unknown exception.
D) It is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The status of a specified general text is disputed among Hanafis: it may remain partially valid or be completely nullified like an unknown exception.

Three Positions on the General Term after Specification
Debates the validity of a general term after specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions regarding the general term after specification and identify the Hanafi-approved position.

Core Idea
After specification, the general term does not fall entirely nor stay definitive — it remains a probable (zanni) proof.

This passage presents two extreme views within the Hanafi school: one that drops the general term entirely as a proof, and another that keeps it as definitive. The relied-upon Hanafi position lies in between, treating the general as a probable proof after specification. Understanding this debate reveals the school's nuanced approach to textual evidence and the use of analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two extreme positions
Read the passage and list what al-Karkhi and Isa ibn Aban hold (second madhhab) versus the third madhhab. The second drops the general completely; the third keeps it as it was, even definitive.
2
Analyze the analogies used
The second madhhab analogizes the specifier to an unknown exception (istithna majhul). The third analogizes to an abrogator (nasikh). Understand how each analogy supports its extreme.
3
Examine the fiqh example
The sale of a slave and a free person for one price is used to illustrate the positions. According to the second view, the free person's presence voids the entire sale; according to the third, it does not affect the slave's sale. See how the analogy translates into a ruling.
4
Determine the moderate Hanafi position
The text hints at the moderate view: the general after specification remains a proof (hujja) but becomes zanni (probable), avoiding both extremes. This is the relied-upon position in the school.

بيان العام المخصوص
هذا العام المخصوص وقيل إنه يسقط الاحتجاج به كالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأن كل واحد منهما لبيان أنه لم يدخل، هو المذهب الثاني، وإليه ذهب الكرخي وعيسى بن أبان، وهؤلاء قد فرطوا في هذا العام المخصوص البعض، ويقولون : لا يبقى العام قابلاً للتمسك أصلاً، سواء كان المخصوص معلومًا كما إذا قيل: اقتلوا المشركين ولا تقتلوا أهل الذمة"، أو مجهولاً كما إذا قيل: "اقتلوا المشركين ولا تقتلوا بعضهم، وشبهوه بالاستثناء فقط؛ لأنهم لم يراعوا جانب الصيغة بل اعتبروا المعنى فقط وهو عدم الدخول، وإنما شبهوه بالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأنه إذا كان دليل المخصوص مجهولا، فظاهر أنه كالمجهول وإن كان معلومًا، فبالتعليل لا بالناسخ أي كالاستثناء يصير مجهولاً، وإن كان الاستثناء في نفسه مما لا يقبل التعليل. فصار كالبيع المضاف إلى حرّ و عبد بثمن واحد تشبيه لدليل هذا المذهب بمسألة فقهية مذكورة، فإنه إذا باع العبد والحر بثمن واحد بأن يقول: "بعتهما بالألف،" فالحر لا يدخل في البيع، فيكون استثناء، يسقط إلخ أي لا يبقى العام حجة لا قطعية ولا ظنية كالاستثناء إلخ يعني أن المخصص كالاستثناء المجهول، وجهالة الاستثناء توجب جهالة المستثنى منه، فيكون الباقي مجهولاً، فكذا جهالة المخصص توجب جهالة العام، فلا يبقى العام حجة. لأن كل واحد إلخ: دليل للإلحاق المستفاد من كاف التشبيه في قوله كالاستثناء المجهول أي إنما ألحق المخصص بالاستثناء المجهول؛ لأن كل واحد منهما أي من المخصص والاستثناء المجهول لبيان إلخ، فالاستثناء يبين أن المستثنى لم يدخل في صدر الكلام، فكذا المخصص يدل على أن المخصوص لم يدخل تحت العام. (القمر) وإنما شبهوه إلخ : دفع دخل تقريره أن تشبيه العام المخصوص منه بالاستثناء المجهول صحيح إذا كان الخصوص أي المخصص مجهولاً، وأما إذا كان معلوماً، فلا، وتقرير الدفع ظاهر. (السنبلي فبالتعليل إلخ يعني أن المخصص المعلوم لاستقلاله يقبل التعليل، ولم يعرف أن أي قدر خرج، فصار المخرج مجهولاً، فبقي الباقي مجهولاً. (القمر) مما لا يقبل التعليل: لأن الاستثناء ليس بنص مستقل، بل بمنزلة وصف قائم بفحوى الكلام دال على عدم دخول المستثنى منه والعدم لا يعلل. (المحشي)
